The King Wishes Him Success, the American President Wishes Him a Safe Journey

Japan Takes Another Step to Intensify Its Annexation Plan; Northeast Telecommunications Falls Entirely into Japanese Hands 36

Xie Jieshi Signs a Treacherous Contract with Mutō

(Changchun) The (puppet) "Manchukuo" and Japan have signed a contract to jointly operate the telecommunications and transportation businesses in the Kwantung Leased Territory, the South Manchurian Railway Zone, and other places in "Manchukuo." The Manchu representative is Xie Jieshi, and the Japanese representative is Mutō. It is heard that the required capital will be determined by the governments and the people of both countries. This contract will take effect after it is approved by the governments of both countries. (15th Reuters Telegram)

(Nanjing) The Japan-Manchu agreement on the Manchurian electric communication business, which was negotiated by Ambassador Mutō and the (puppet) "Manchukuo Foreign Minister," was formally signed on March 26th of this year and announced simultaneously in Tokyo and Changchun at 4 p.m. on the 15th. The content is as follows: Electric communication business is the nervous system of a country, which is not only of great importance, but also has an important role in the development of culture and economy. However, the Manchurian electric communication business, which is operated by the Japanese side in the Kwantung Prefecture and the South Manchurian Railway Affiliated Area, and the electric communication business operated by "Manchukuo" within the territory of "Manchukuo," means that two communication businesses are opposed to each other in the same area, so there are many regrets in the connection, and there are also disadvantages of double investment of capital, which also leads to useless competition, which is a great hindrance to the development of the business of "Manchukuo." The governments of Japan and Manchu recognized the necessity of merging all electric communication facilities in Manchu of the two countries, and on March 26, Showa 8, the Japanese representative Ambassador Mutō and the "Manchukuo" representative Xie "Foreign Minister" signed and sealed the agreement, stipulating that the electric communication facilities of Japan in the Kwantung Prefecture and the South Manchurian Railway Affiliated Area and the electric communication facilities owned by "Manchukuo" should be merged, and civilian capital should be added to form a Japan-Manchu joint communication company. "The Manchukuo Government" has the intention to respect various debts concerning this company. This agreement will be approved in both countries after being signed by the representatives, and the text of the agreement will be published after the exchange of the approval documents. (15th Joint Telegram)

Lytton Criticizes Churchill as Being Senile! 47

Those Who Love the League of Nations Should Not Avoid Difficulties

The Sino-Japanese Problem Should Be Resolved in Accordance with the League Covenant

(London) Conservative Party member Churchill recently gave a speech in which he said that the League of Nations had made a big mistake by interfering in the Sino-Japanese dispute. When Lord Lytton spoke in Reading, he refuted Churchill's remarks. Lord Lytton said, "I have read Churchill's advice to the League of Nations not to interfere in the Sino-Japanese dispute. Churchill claims that he respects the League of Nations, supports the League of Nations, and sincerely hopes that the League of Nations will succeed, so he does not want to see the League of Nations being dragged into the Sino-Japanese problem. This kind of view is really strange in the eyes of friends of the League of Nations. I am afraid that Churchill is gradually becoming senile. I have known Churchill for a long time, and I have never seen him shrink back from difficulties. He has dealt with difficult undertakings in various political parties in Britain." (The audience laughed, because Churchill has repeatedly changed parties.) "I have never known Churchill to advise his friends to escape from difficulties, but I did not expect that Churchill is now advising the League of Nations to abandon difficulties out of love for the League of Nations. In fact, the only solution we can seek for the Sino-Japanese problem is not to escape from difficulties, but to deal with difficulties in accordance with the League of Nations covenant. We must support any solution agreed upon by the League of Nations." (Reuters News Agency)

A Daylight Robbery in the Capital; A Construction Factory Was Robbed of More Than 7,400 Yuan 48

Police in All Districts Conduct a Four-Sided Roundup

Two Policemen Die, Two Thieves Are Captured

(Nanjing) At 3:30 p.m. on the 15th, Wang Rongji Construction Factory in Dafengfu Lane, Xinjiekou, received 7,497 yuan in construction fees for building school buildings for the Engineering and Artillery Schools. All of the money was in Central Bank notes. They immediately used the telephone to notify various material factories to come and collect the material fees. While they were calculating the accounts, four thieves broke in one after another, using a pistol to cut the telephone line and scaring Wang Qifa and the men and women in the house, forbidding them to make any noise. All of the 7,497 yuan that had been received was robbed, and then they fled together. At this time, the police on duty at the Shigulu Sub-Bureau of the Fifth Police Bureau heard the news, urgently sounded the police whistle, and gathered police to pursue the thieves. Led by Police Chief Chen Zhengeng, more than 20 policemen followed and chased the thieves. One policeman chased the thieves to the front of the Anti-Opium Commission. Because his gun malfunctioned, he was resisted by the thieves and shot to death. The remaining policemen bravely advanced. Subsequently, the police on duty at the First Bureau on Zhongshan Road sounded the police whistle to conduct a roundup. Another policeman was shot to death by the thieves, and one policeman was injured. At this time, police teams from all districts gathered and captured two thieves on the spot. One was Wu Jiayou, 26 years old, from Hefei, who was carrying a Brownie pistol. The other was Zhou Peiwen, 25 years old, from Huaicheng. They were escorted to the Fifth Bureau by Chen Wensheng, a patrol officer from the Shigulu Sub-Bureau, and then transferred to the police station for interrogation. The policeman who was shot to death in front of the Anti-Opium Commission was Cao Deshan, a petitioner policeman from the Shigulu Sub-Bureau of the Fifth Bureau, from Suqian. One policeman who died was Wang Wenyu, a policeman from the Yangpixiang Sub-Bureau of the First Bureau, from Hebei Province, who was shot in the chest. He was rushed to the hospital by streetcar, but died on the way to Daxinggong. The injured policeman's name is Wu Wanhai, also from Hebei Province. He was shot twice by the thieves, one shot entering his left arm and one bullet entering his lungs. He was immediately taken to the Second Hospital of the Central Hospital for treatment. According to the person in charge of the police, four robbers have been arrested in this case, two policemen have been shot dead by the robbers, and two policemen have been injured. More than 1,700 yuan in cash was found on one robber. After the incident, Police Chief Chen Zhuo personally went to the scene to investigate. Chen advocated giving preferential treatment and rewards to the policemen who died in the line of duty and were injured. The police station will interrogate the arrested robbers overnight in order to pursue the remaining accomplices. (15th Special Dispatch)

In addition, after the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, the import of Russian goods is very prosperous, with kerosene and timber being the most numerous, exceeding the value of our country's exports to Russia several times. Gold Rises, Silver is Hit. The United States Will Lift the Gold Embargo. 78

Secretary of the Treasury Woodin Opposes Inflationary Currency and Devaluation of Gold Prices

New York Bank Exports a Batch of Gold to the Netherlands

National Press, Washington, 14th - Sources close to the government tonight claim that Treasury Secretary Woodin will oppose printing more money or devaluing the US dollar under any circumstances. Most financiers believe this means that President Roosevelt will also hold the same view. The inflationary currency faction in Congress will temporarily cease activities, at least until after the World Economic Conference. The rapid advance of the movement to devalue the gold dollar in Congress and the rapid decline of the US dollar in foreign markets reached a point on Thursday where action had to be taken. Therefore, the government approved the export of a batch of gold by a New York bank to the Netherlands for rescue. Now, members of Congress and financial experts believe that the US president will also make a clear statement on the issue of inflationary currency in the coming days.

National Press, Washington, 14th - After the US dollar experienced a depreciation in foreign exchange markets unseen for many years, the Federal Reserve today announced that a New York bank had obtained a license to ship gold to the Netherlands. However, the amount of gold and the name of the bank were not disclosed. It is said that this move by the authorities is to avoid further depreciation of the US dollar in foreign markets.

Although today is a holiday, many financiers still went to their offices to read the latest reports, and many claimed that they anticipated the gold embargo would be lifted soon, or at least a part of it. Because the value of the US dollar must be strongly maintained in the coming days, even a small amount of gold shipped abroad will be enough to curb the dollar's depreciation. Considering the recent situation in the financial sector, it may be possible to allow several more batches of gold to be shipped out. Therefore, the financial community is paying attention to the US president's actions to prevent further depreciation of the dollar. The activities of the silver and inflationary currency factions in the US Congress, and the news that the Canadian Prime Minister will discuss the possibility of resetting the value of gold in the world with the US President, have greatly impacted the dollar. Therefore, observers here believe that unless the gold embargo is largely lifted, the only option is to allow the dollar to depreciate further. Economists generally believe that if the US President can take immediate action to curb the dollar's depreciation, it can be regarded as an expression of his attitude towards inflationary currency. Since taking office, the US President has not made any other statements regarding currency, except to state the need for a suitable supply of stable currency.

As for the Federal Reserve Bank's gold reserve report, it increased by $8,700,000 yesterday. In the week ending on the 12th, it had already increased by $8,397,000. The reason for both increases was due to the decrease in the amount in foreign gold accounts, and the import of gold from China, Latin America, Australia, and other countries. China imported $102,000, Australia imported $267,000, and Latin American countries imported a total of $31,000. Therefore, under these circumstances, the gold embargo seems to be eased somewhat.

The US Plan to Save the Economic Decline Requires Issuing 600 Billion Yuan in Public Debt 79

National Press, Washington, 14th - Labor Secretary Perkins told the Senate Agriculture Committee that the government plans to use a joint plan to relieve unemployment and rural areas to save the economic decline, which is estimated to require the issuance of 600 billion yuan in public debt. However, only half of the required amount will be needed in the next six months. She also asked cities to engage in public works in cooperation with the government, and said that she had received more than 2,000 relief plans from the people, many of which contained good suggestions, demonstrating the nation's attention to this matter and everyone's willingness to cooperate with the government.

Moscow Court Continues Trial of British Engineers 80

Soviet Judge Deems MacDonald's Confession Valid

Russian Manager Says the Case is Fabricated

Reuters, Moscow, 14th - The British engineers case opened for its third day of hearing today. Although MacDonald recanted his confession and pleaded not guilty, the judge deemed his original confession valid. A key point of the day was whether the 3,000 rubles given by Thornton to Russian engineer Mrs. Durgov was a loan or a bribe. Durgov claimed that she regarded this amount as an improper gift, so she turned it over to the authorities, and she had a clear conscience. Although Ms. Durgov believed this, her frank answers made a good impression. Thornton claimed that it was a loan, but he did not issue a receipt because Ms. Durgov said that a receipt was not necessary. The court then questioned MacDonald and Nordwall about their admission of negligence in the indictment. Kortlelevsky, head of the turbine room of the Soviet Sugar Factory, said that at MacDonald's request, he threw a large nail into the generator and damaged the motor, for which MacDonald paid him 1,000 rubles. He also gave MacDonald a drawing of the Soviet Sugar Factory. Other witnesses said that Nordwall instigated them to be negligent, and they followed his instructions. One witness said that Nordwall had given 5,000 rubles. Nordwall was greatly surprised to hear this testimony and immediately declared to the court that all this testimony was false. The court also questioned the sale of leather clothing between Nordwall and a certain witness. Nordwall claimed that the leather clothing belonged to another British engineer, who asked him to sell it to a certain witness, get the cash, and forward it to the owner. Prosecutor Vishinsky heavily criticized Nordwall for the slight discrepancies between his testimony today and the confession he had prepared before the trial. Laitek, the administrative head of the Soviet government, also attended the hearing today.

After a three-hour recess, Nordwall was called to the stand again for questioning. Nordwall's answers were brief and firm, making a very good impression. Allenik, a Russian employee of Vickers, answered the court's questions, saying that Nordwall should be responsible for the improper installation of a certain turbine because Nordwall did not notice the errors in the blueprints. Nordwall immediately argued that he had not seen any errors, and even the expert committee had not discovered them. He had no malicious intent. A Russian named Xue Bait, who testified in court, said that he had never worked for Vickers, but he was friendly with Thornton. Thornton told him that the company's machinery was very sophisticated and that there was no need for excessive inspections. He found defects in the switch, which prevented the work from being carried out quickly, and told Thornton, who thanked him and gave him 300 rubles. Thornton heard this and immediately stood up to deny it, saying that he had given Xue Bait 250 rubles, which was a bonus because Xue's work was good. Xue Bait also claimed that he respected Thornton and believed his words, so he began to be negligent. He also claimed that the British defendant Gregory made anti-Soviet propaganda after arriving in Dnipropetrovsk. Gregory was a British Welshman and a Vickers installation technician. After hearing Xue's testimony, he spoke loudly and vehemently, saying, "This person insults me and ruins my reputation, and the judge listens to him without questioning him. Is this fair?" The judge stopped him, saying, "Speak on the facts, now is not the time for you to speak." Gregory then continued to speak, saying that he went to Dnipropetrovsk to install oil engines, and he worked very carefully in order to maintain the company's reputation. Gregory then turned to the expert committee sitting in a corner of the courtroom and said, "I installed three oil engines, each weighing 45 tons, in 48 days. Please judge whether my work was good."

I do not understand Russian, how can I do propaganda to the workers? I have no time to guide the Russians in their work, and I never pay attention to politics. The last witness was Sokolukin, the deputy chief technician of the Moscow power plant, also one of the defendants, who said that he had received 2,500 rubles from Thornton as a negligence fee. Thornton instructed him to destroy the main power plant during the war in order to sabotage the Russian electrical industry. Thornton and he had jointly agreed on a negligence plan. Thornton immediately denied having had this conversation and denied having bribed him. The trial adjourned at 10 p.m. tonight.

Borodin was also one of those who attended the hearing.

Reuters, Moscow, 15th - The trial of six British Vickers employees and twelve Russian employees accused of bribery, espionage, and negligence resumed this morning. As soon as the court opened, Monkhouse, the Russian manager of Vickers, stood up and said, "I want to say something. I have been interrogated for 18 hours. I dare to say that this case is fabricated. After hearing Sokolukin's testimony yesterday, I am willing to prove that this case is based on the confessions of Russians who have been threatened." When Mr. Monkhouse said this, the judge hurriedly stopped him from speaking. A group of people who confessed to negligence then came to court to be questioned. Krasheninnikov, chief technician of the Moscow Electric Power Plant, claimed that the Vickers machinery did have defects, but he was instructed not to report them, so he did not report them. Monkhouse interjected and said, "I admit that the machinery did have some defects, but I do not believe that Krasheninnikov was negligent." K replied, "But I believe that I was negligent." Another Russian employee of the Moscow Electric Power Plant, Solin, testified that Thornton gave him 1,000 rubles and asked him to be negligent. Thornton's expression did not change when he heard this. The judge announced today that the trial could be completed tomorrow.

Reuters, Moscow, 14th - British engineer MacDonald initially confessed to his guilt during the trial, then recanted, and most recently confessed again, his position is very confusing. Yesterday, during the recess, the court handed MacDonald over to the Political Detective Bureau for custody. After this, MacDonald's actions changed suddenly. According to a report on the trial situation released by British officialdom, MacDonald's expression was obviously different when he re-entered the courtroom. When the court asked again if he had engaged in espionage, MacDonald replied in a low voice, "Yes, I did," and admitted that he had issued instructions to destroy machinery. However, in any case, according to Soviet Russian law, MacDonald cannot be convicted until all the evidence has been fully examined.

Reuters, London, 14th - The board of directors of Vickers Electrical Company held a meeting today and unanimously passed a resolution expressing sympathy for the British employees in Russia who are being tried, and expressing confidence in their integrity and loyalty. The board also decided to elect Mr. Richard of the company's Russian business to the board of directors, in order to show the company's trust in Mr. Richard.

After Mussolini Initiates the Four-Power Pact, Italy Seems to be the Hegemon of Central Europe 81

Papen and Goering Strive for German-Italian Cooperation in Rome

The Austrian Chancellor is also Said to be Conducting a Movement to Distance Himself from Germany and Get Close to Italy

National Press, Rome, 14th - German Vice-Chancellor Papen and Prussian Prime Minister Goering met with Italian journalists today. Papen said that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's peace efforts, as expressed in the Four-Power Pact he proposed, have won the sympathy of the entire German public opinion. Goering said that he and Papen both sincerely hope that Germany and Italy can cooperate closely, and that there are no differences between the two countries that can separate them. Goering has left Italy by plane for Syracuse, Sicily, and is accompanied by Prince Hess, the leader of the German National Socialist Party in Italy.

Havas, Vienna, 15th - Chancellor Dollfuss, speaking to reporters from the Berliner Tageblatt about the Four-Power Pact, said that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and British Prime Minister MacDonald were doing their best to build a new era of peace, and that Austria would always support the avoidance of war, and that it was also necessary to avoid misunderstandings on other issues. Chancellor Du then explained the significance of Italian Prime Minister raising his glass at a banquet in Rome to celebrate the future of an independent Austria, saying that it was to celebrate the future of the Austrian Constitution and its republican system. Du concluded, "From now on, I know that Austria has gained a true ally in the South."

Havas, Vienna, 15th - Austrian Interior Minister and Deputy Chancellor Winkler issued a statement to the press saying that negotiations on the issue of concluding a preferential tariff agreement with Germany will continue on May 10. Continuing to talk about internal affairs, Winkler criticized the German National Socialist Party's propaganda to boycott Austrian spas. Regarding the issue of creditors of Austria's lending bank, Winkler said that negotiations will continue after Easter. Winkler also stated that the Austrian government has no intention of holding new elections at present, nor will it reorganize the cabinet. As for the 5,000 newly recruited auxiliary police, they will be trained by officers from the federal army. The training period is four weeks, and they will be dismissed after the period expires, and then reconvened when necessary. Winkler also said that the various speculations about Chancellor Dollfuss's previous trip to Rome were completely unfounded.

Havas, Vienna, 14th - Foreign newspapers are quite uneasy about the restoration of the Habsburg dynasty and the reconstruction of the Austro-Hungarian Federation. The Neue Freie Presse here published an article saying, "The Austrians all hope that Austria and Hungary can compromise with each other, but if the restoration plan is put forward, it will inevitably be defeated due to German opposition. Although Italy is friendly to both Austria and Hungary, it will never lose Germany's favor because of this."

Havas, Prague, 15th - Czech newspapers have adopted an extremely reserved attitude towards the recent talks in Rome. It is generally believed that the Italian side wants Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss to expand the scope of the coalition cabinet to include Hitler's party members, and on the one hand wants to make the Berlin government guarantee Austria's independence. The Czech side opposes the German-Austrian union and the restoration of the Austro-Hungarian Empire, and remains waiting and watching.

He met a former comrade-in-arms in Russia who guided him back to his country. German political circles are deeply displeased that British Foreign Secretary Simon did not criticize such remarks.

Havas, London, 15th - The Times commented on the speeches made by some members of Parliament against Germany during the House of Commons discussion on foreign policy on Thursday, saying that the sympathy that Germany had aroused in Britain in the past ten or twelve years has been lost in recent weeks. Cuban Terrorist Movement 84

Havana dispatch, 14th: The Cuban revolutionary party's terrorist campaign, which began in February, has intensified daily. Today, there were as many as nineteen bombing incidents. This morning, non-official secret agents of the current government seized two youths, drove them in a car to the outskirts, ordered them out, and forced them to run between two rows of armed secret agents. One was then seen to die from serious injuries, and the other also fell to the ground, whereupon they were abandoned. After the bombing incidents occurred, the government warned defense forces everywhere to watch for aircraft attempting to fly in from neighboring islands to bomb. Tonight's news is that the newly restored constitutional guarantees in five provinces will be temporarily lifted again. Recently, in Cuba, bombing incidents, sugar mill arsons, train derailments or bombings, village robberies, or attacks on military forces have occurred almost daily. Because of the strict inspections by the military authorities, newspapers are largely unable to report them.

Reuters, Havana dispatch, 14th: There were no fewer than seventeen bombing incidents today, resulting in one death and multiple injuries. Previously, the police department received an anonymous letter stating that Havana's "Red Week" would begin yesterday, requiring police vigilance. As a result, the police searched everywhere for people with violent tendencies and those suspected of opposing President Machado. They then dispatched cavalry to patrol the streets, and all cars driving in the city were forced to stop at gunpoint and searched. Police arrested dozens of young people, including three students of unknown origin, all of whom were sent to a certain place for detention. Police patrols are now carrying machine guns to prevent further incidents. Today, a bomb exploded not far from the residence of the former Ambassador to the United States, now State Councilor, Ferreira. The bomb was hidden in a fruit vendor's cart, killing a three-year-old child and seriously injuring three others. Police saw a nineteen-year-old youth placing a bomb on a street corner, and when they approached to arrest him, the youth fled but was shot down. His life is feared to be in danger.

The Military Bearing of the 19th Route Army Aiding Jehol 85

Enthusiastic Farewell from the Populace in Counties Passed

Student Soldiers Also Accompany the Camp Northward to Resist Japan

Shantou Correspondence: The 19th Route Army's troops aiding Jehol, totaling two columns, are divided into [blank] regiments. Artillery, engineering, logistics, and communications troops are all fully equipped. The commander of the First Column, Yan, is currently in Guangzhou, having traveled by sea after the detachment's departure. His unit is commanded by Chief of Staff Li Kuo. They left Longyan on March 27th, entered Guangdong Province at Kan City, Dabu, and arrived at Shiyun District on the 30th, going directly to Fenglang, Tongren, and Sanheba. The populace along the way enthusiastically bid them farewell. Dabu County Magistrate Liang Ruogu personally went to Sanheba to welcome them and prepared four electric boats to transport military supplies to Songkou. All circles in Dabu specially presented four banners, inscribed "Achieve Merit and Subdue the Barbarians," "The Party and the Nation Depend on You," "Restore Our Rivers and Mountains," and "Light of the Nation." They arrived in Songkou on April 1st. Meixian County Magistrate Peng Jingyi first sent a car to Songkou to welcome them. Li Kuo and the unit's personnel arrived in Meicheng at 4 PM on the 1st. The infantry battalion camped at Baiduwei that night and began to arrive gradually on the 2nd. All circles in Meixian held a grand welcoming ceremony and presented goods to reward the troops. The unit rested in Mei for two days and set off for Xingning on the 4th. The regimental commanders were Liu Hanzhong and Xie Dingxin. The firearms of these two regiments were sharp, and the uniforms were neat. The Second Column, commanded by Tan Qixiu, departed from Zhangzhou on March 25th. Tan also first went to Guangzhou by sea to discuss all matters related to the march. His unit was commanded by Chief of Staff Rong. They passed through Shancheng, arrived at Xiaoxi on the 26th, arrived at Xiazai on the 27th, arrived at Pinghe on the 28th, and camped at Baihou, Dabu, Guangdong Province, on the 29th. They rested for one day on the 30th, arrived at Sanheba on March 31st, arrived at Songkou on April 1st, rested for one day, and advanced towards Meixian City on the 3rd, joining the First Column. The First Column set off from the Mei-Xing Highway via Nankouwei to Xingning on the 4th, while the Second Column rested in Meicheng. Commander Huang Yanzhen of the 7th Division stationed in Mei specially sent Liang Baoluo, Ouyang Feng, and others to take care of everything. They had designated the 19th Route Army's garrison location in advance, and the reception arrangements along the way were quite thorough. When the First Column departed from Mei, about 16,000 students from Meixian Provincial Fifth Middle School, Dongshan Middle School, County Middle School, Leyu Middle School, Guangyi Middle School, and various boys' and girls' schools sang military songs and bid farewell to Gutangping Airfield, eight li from the city. The sound of firecrackers and heroic songs shook the clear sky. The Second Column continued to arrive in Meicheng on the morning of the 4th. On this day, all agencies, groups, and schools in Meixian were also very busy welcoming them. Those who went to welcome them gathered at the Meisong Road Main Station at Beimengang in the morning. The unit began to arrive completely at 2 PM. The welcomers set off firecrackers. Chief of Staff Rong and the First Regiment Commander Yang Changhuang and Second Regiment Commander Wu Luxun shook hands with each representative in the welcome pavilion at the station as a courtesy. At about 4 PM, all circles carried the gifts of appreciation to each regiment and battalion and distributed them to the soldiers separately. The County Party Department presented a banner inscribed "Restore Our Rivers and Mountains," the 7th Division Headquarters presented a banner inscribed "Resist Japan and Save the Nation," and all circles presented a banner inscribed "Kill the Enemy to the End." The Second Column's officers and soldiers numbered more than one thousand more than the First Column. Chief of Staff Rong's wife, Ms. Xu, Chief Medical Officer Peng's wife, Ms. Pan, and female propaganda nurses were all dressed in military uniforms and served with the army, full of patriotism. In addition, there were about seventy student soldiers who had served in the Songhu Battle and students from Feng Yong University. Many other university and middle school students also abandoned their studies to follow the army. They had all joined the training regiment after entering Fujian with the 19th Route Army last summer and received military training. It is said that they have graduated, so they accompanied the camp northward to resist Japan. In addition, there were engineering teams, heavy artillery teams, anti-aircraft artillery teams, communications teams, and medical teams. From the 5th to the 6th, the First Column began to advance towards Xingning. The Eastern District Pacification Commissioner's Office has notified the county magistrates of Longchuan, Heping, and Lianping to take good care of them along the way. (April 10th)

Song's Training Regiment Moves from Fenyang to the Front Line 86

Passing Through Taiyuan En Route to Zhangjiakou

Led by Regiment Commander Zhi Yinglin

Enthusiastic Farewell from the Populace Along the Way

Taiyuan Correspondence: Since 1919, guest troops stationed in Jin territory have recently been ordered to the front line one after another due to the outbreak of war with Japan. Apart from Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, Sun Dianying, and other major units, only part of Sun Dianying's unit is currently stationed in Jincheng. The unit of [blank] Gang Zhangrenjie stationed in Jiexiu has also been led by Fang Zhenwu to Hebei Province, heading north along the Pinghan Line. The training regiment of Song Zheyuan's unit stationed in Fenyang has also been ordered to move to Zhangjiakou, led by Regiment Commander Zhi Yinglin. It departed on the 10th and arrived in Taiyuan last night (11th). Today (12th), it will depart for Datong and transfer to Zhangjiakou. This regiment was reorganized from Feng Yuxiang's former guard unit. Military discipline is strict, uniforms are neat, and morale is extremely high. The populace of each county passed along the way enthusiastically welcomed them and presented gifts. The gifts included 11,600 yuan from the entire populace of Fenyang County, a large silk banner from He Fen Middle School, a large rectangular red banner from Mingyi Middle School, one hundred handgun bullets from the Public Security Bureau Chief, a large rectangular red banner from County Magistrate Han Mingfu, two large silk banners from the Finance Bureau, Public Security Bureau, Education Bureau, Construction Bureau, and Chamber of Commerce, two large rectangular red banners from Christian schools and organizations, one hundred and twenty pairs of socks from the textile factory, and a satin banner and one hundred towels from Mr. Zhang Fanwu and others. The gifts of money included 5,000 yuan from the entire populace of Wenshui County, 4,000 yuan from the entire populace of Jiaocheng County, 2,000 yuan from the entire populace of Qingyuan County, and 1,000 yuan from the entire populace of Taiyuan County. The regiment also issued a declaration of departure, about a thousand words long, explaining that the departure was to assist the soldiers of the 29th and 41st Armies in resisting Japan, and stating that to overthrow imperialism, it is necessary not only for our army but also to mobilize the revolutionary masses of the whole country to participate in this great and arduous war in order to achieve victory. Now we are going to the front line, and we hope that all circles of the country will come to the front line. Now is the critical moment for the survival of the Chinese nation. Non-resistance means death. We must muster our courage and strive for China's independence and unity. The regiment also issued a public notice along the way, which stated that since Jehol has fallen, the enemy's arrogance has become more intense. The officers and soldiers of this unit are all pained by the brutality of the Japanese invaders and are mindful of the imminent national demise. They are determined to kill the enemy and have already made a resolution. This time, they are ordered to go north and rush to the battlefield, fulfilling their duty as soldiers. However, fearing that people from all walks of life are unaware of the truth and may be alarmed by the army's presence, a clear notice is hereby issued. The discipline of this army has always been extremely strict. Public purchases and sales will be made in the places it passes through, and the people will never be disturbed. If there are unscrupulous soldiers or local ruffians who use the name of this army to spread rumors and cause trouble, merchants and people are permitted to immediately arrest them and send them to this headquarters for severe punishment according to the law, without any leniency. Let all circles of people be fully informed. Sincerely, this notice. (April 12th)

Dai Yue Recovers Xingan 87

Bandit Gangs Focus on Attacking Fuzhou

Liu Zhi Attacks the Main Force of the Bandits

The Situation on the Gan River is Easing

Nanchang Correspondence: The Chinese Communists (Red Bandits) have launched an all-out attack this time. The plan of the counterfeit military committee is to have the counterfeit central army, the 1st, 3rd, and 5th Army Corps, as the central route, gathering at Yihuang and Lean to attack Fuzhou; the counterfeit Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Fujian Military Region's Fang Shao's counterfeit 10th Army, 30th, 31st, 32nd and other divisions, leaving Xinhe and attacking Jinxi and Dongxiang as the right route; and scattered bandits on the east and west banks of the Gan River, gathered at Yongfeng and Xiajiang, led by Mao Zedong, going down the Gan River and the Gan-Yue Road, attempting to seize Zhangshu as the left route. After Fuzhou is captured, the three routes will then conspire to seize Nanchang. All of the above forces are commanded by the counterfeit commander-in-chief Zhu De. However, among the bandits' three routes this time, they are completely focused on Fuzhou. On the Xin River front, Fang's bandits have only three or four thousand rifles. Although they attacked and captured Dongxiang County on the 11th at Majiawei, on the Jinxi-Linchuan border, it is irrelevant to the overall war situation. The Mao bandits on the east bank of the Gan River occasionally send plainclothes teams to invade the vicinity of Zhangshu, but they only repeatedly harass to create a diversion, cover the main force, and attempt to seize Fuzhou. President Chiang Kai-shek had already seen through the bandits' cunning scheme, so he specially ordered Liu Zhi to go to Fuzhou to supervise the war on his behalf, leading the central route's various columns to attack the bandits' main force. On the Xin River front, Zhang Zhizhong's division has recently arrived, and Dongxiang can be recovered soon. On the Gan River front, in addition to Chen Cheng and other units firmly defending the Qiqin-Mifeng area bordering Chongren, Fengcheng, Lean, and Xingan to prevent the bandits from flanking Fuzhou, and Sun Lianzhong's unit resolutely defending Yongfeng City to contain the bandits' main force, Dai Yue's unit, which recently arrived in Jiangxi, is advancing upstream along the Gan River and the Gan-Yue Road from Zhangshu. Yesterday (12th), they defeated Luo Binghui's counterfeit 22nd Army in the Yongtai area below Xingan and above Jijiang, and pursued them in victory. A phone call was received from Zhangshu a moment ago stating that Dai's unit had recovered Xingan County today (13th), and the counterfeit 21st, 22nd Army, and Independent 4th and 5th Divisions had scattered and retreated to Yongfeng, Lean, Xiajiang, and other places. The situation on the Gan River has therefore eased, and Zhangshu has also turned from danger to safety. It is heard that Chiang, in order to quickly suppress the Red Bandits, has added large armies from Guangdong, Guangxi, Hunan, Henan, and other provinces into Jiangxi, and has dispatched the 4th Squadron of fighters stationed in Hankou, eight Jiangkun and Jiangxi warships, one after another to Jiangxi, in order to coordinate with the military operations, so the future of bandit suppression is [blank]. (April 13th)

Record of the Chen-Peng Case Trial 88

Chen and Peng Admit Without Hesitation to Being Central Committee Members of the Communist Party

But Ultimately Refuse to Acknowledge Endangering the Republic

Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, and Pu Yifan, Wang Wu (i.e., Song Fengchun), Wang Ziping, He Afang, Wang Zhaoqun, Guo Jinghao (i.e., Peng Daozhi), Liang Youguang, Wang Jianying, and Wang Xiaochun, eleven leaders of the Trotskyist faction of the Chinese Communist Party, were arrested in Shanghai last October and transferred to the Jiangning District Court Detention Center for custody. After the Jiangsu High Court sent prosecutor Zhu [blank] to open the case for investigation, Chen, Peng, and the other ten were prosecuted for endangering the Republic, except for Wang Xiaochun, who was released without charge. The public trial was held at 9 AM on the 14th in the criminal court of the Jiangning District Court. Chen and the other two admitted without hesitation to being Communist Party leaders. A record of the situation is as follows:

Circumstances of the Public Trial 89

The Jiangsu High Court, considering that Chen, Peng, and others were all important figures of the Trotskyist faction of the Chinese Communist Party, specially requested the Police Department of the [blank] Ministry to send a platoon of armed security guards to the Jiangning District Court on the morning of the 14th to be on alert. Because this case caused a sensation at the time, as many as eighty or ninety people went to observe. At 9:45 AM, presiding judge Hu Shan [blank], judges Lin Zhemin and Zhang Bingci, clerk Shen Yuren, prosecutor Zhu [blank], and others ascended the courtroom. The defense lawyers for Chen, Peng, and others, Zhang Shizhao, Wu Zhiping, Peng Wanglin, Jiang Haoshi, Liu Zuwang, and other five people, also arrived one after another. Judge Hu then summoned Chen, Peng, and the other ten to the court, asking each of their names, ages, places of origin, addresses, and occupations. They were then returned to the waiting room and Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, Pu Yifan, Wang Wu, and others were questioned individually. Chen Duxiu was wearing a blue cloth long gown and cloth cotton robe, and Peng Shuzhi was wearing a gray cloth cotton robe. During the questioning, their attitudes were calm and composed. At times, witty remarks arose, causing laughter throughout the court. The court adjourned at 1:30 PM. At 9 AM on the 15th, the trial of the remaining defendants continued.

Prosecutor's Public Indictment 90

After summoning the defendants to the court, the prosecutor first stood up to present the public indictment, stating briefly: "In October of last year, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, based on a confidential report, stated that on the upper floor of No. 210 Chunyang Lane, Dongyouheng Road, Public Concession, there was a counterfeit central organ of the Communist Party. The Bureau immediately dispatched inspectors Tang Bao and Zhang Qingtai, holding a letter to issue a search and arrest warrant from the First Special District Court, together with Detective Gower and Detective Clerk of the Patrol Force, and others, to go to the address at 3 PM on the 15th of the same month. Xie Shaoshan and the defendants Pu Yifan, Peng Shuzhi (i.e., Zhang Cinan), Wang Wu (i.e., Song Fengchun), Wang Zhao [blank], and other five people were holding a meeting, so they were arrested together. A large number of reactionary documents were seized at the scene, as well as several pieces of paper with communication addresses. The detectives then, based on this location, went to the upper floor of No. 11 Yongxing Lane, Yuezhou Road, at 7 PM on the same day, and arrested the defendant Chen Duxiu, and seized a large number of reactionary documents. At about 9 PM, they searched the home of Pu Yifan at No. 322 Gaofu Lane, Shengmuyuan Road, seized various reactionary documents, and arrested Wang Xiaochun. At about 12 midnight that night, they went to No. 1044 Siwen Lane, Datong Road. Because it was late at night, the sound of knocking on the door alarmed the people in the lane. Two people jumped out of the window. One escaped, and only the defendant Liang Youguang was arrested, and many reactionary documents were seized. At 7:30 AM on the 16th, at the lower floor of No. 335 Yeguang Lane, Tangshan Road, the defendants Wang Ziping and He Afang were printing the Communist Party publications Spark and School Life. They were arrested together with the evidence. At 12 noon, the defendant Wang Jiantang was arrested at No. 22 Fuqing Lane, and ten kinds of reactionary books were seized. Previously, after the detectives arrested Wang Ziping and others at No. 335 Yeguang Lane, Tangshan Road, they sent people to secretly guard the place. Until the 17th, the defendant Guo Jinghao (i.e., Peng Daozhi), unaware that the matter had been exposed, went to the place and was also arrested. They were then sent to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau to send them back. Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi were first transferred to the Military Law Department of the Army Department of the Ministry of Military Administration for questioning. They were found to have no connection with the Communist bandits in Hubei, Jiangxi, and other places, and Chen Duxiu and others were not active-duty soldiers, and the crime scene did not comply with the first paragraph of Article 7 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic. It was believed that the Ministry had no jurisdiction, so it was transferred to the Ministry of Justice and Administration for handling according to the law. This office collected evidence and interrogated them repeatedly. Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, and others all admitted without hesitation to joining the Communist Party, founding the Chinese Communist Party Left Opposition faction, and being elected as central committee members. While the investigation was in progress, it was learned that the Public Concession Patrol Force had also subsequently seized more than forty kinds of reactionary documents in Chen Duxiu's home. A member was sent to the Central Party Headquarters to collect them all, and the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau was requested to transfer the co-defendants Wang Wu (i.e., Song Fengchun), Pu Yifan, Wang Ziping, He Afang, Wang Zhaoqun, Guo Jinghao, Liang Youguang, Wang Jiantang, Wang Xiaochun, and other nine people to this office for joint trial. As a result of the investigation, except for Wang Xiaochun, who was found to have no conclusive evidence and was given a separate decision not to prosecute, Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi (i.e., Zhang Cinan), Pu Yifan, Wang Wu (i.e., Song Fengchun), Wang Ziping, He Afang, Wang Zhao [blank], Guo Jinghao (i.e., Peng Daozhi), Liang Youguang, and Wang Jiantang organized groups or assemblies for the purpose of endangering the Republic, all violating Article 6 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Crimes Endangering the Republic. In addition, Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi used words to promote treason, and Wang Ziping and He Afang assisted in the promotion of treason, also carrying a great suspicion of violating Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the same law. The seized Communist books and documents are all for criminal use and criminal preparation. Please confiscate them all in accordance with Article 10 of the same law and Article 60, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law. In accordance with Article 253, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, I hereby file a public prosecution."

First, Chen Duxiu is Summoned for Trial 91

After the prosecutor finished reading the indictment, Judge Hu immediately summoned Chen Duxiu for interrogation, asking about his age, place of origin, and occupation. According to Chen Duxiu's statement, he was 55 years old, from Huaining, Anhui. During the fifth and sixth years of the Republic (1916-1917), he was a university professor in Beijing for a total of 23 years. Around the 19th year of the Republic (1930), he went to Shanghai, and in the 11th and 12th years (1922-1923), he went to Guangdong, serving as the Director of the Guangdong Education Department for about a year. After that, he returned to Shanghai and had no occupation. In 1927, he was elected as the Secretary of the Chinese Communist Party, guiding the activities of the Communist Party. During the Nationalist Party's purge of the Communists, he participated in Communist Party work in Wuhan and had no other social activities. (The judge asked) Is the Third International satisfied with you? (Chen replied) Satisfied in some areas, not satisfied in others. (Asked) What kind of position is the Secretary? (Answered) It's the General Secretary, also the Central Chairman. (Asked) When were you expelled from the Communist Party? (Answered) Around the 17th or 18th year of the Republic (1928 or 1929). (Asked) Why were you expelled? (Answered) Due to differences in opinion. (Asked) Where were the differences in opinion? (Answered) These are internal party matters; I don't want to say more. (Asked), (Asked)

Have you worked for the Nationalist Party? (Answered) No, I haven't before the purge of the Communists or after I was expelled. I haven't done anything. (Asked) What did you do in Shanghai after you were expelled? (Answered) I didn't do anything, nor did I write any books. (Asked) Which faction of the Communist Party do you belong to? (Answered) The Trotskyist faction. (Asked) Is the Communist Party divided into Stalinist and Trotskyist factions? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) What is the situation of the Trotskyist faction? (Answered) The Trotskyist faction doesn't have many members in Russia. Trotsky is the leader. He used to be in Turkey, and now he's there, but because I don't read the newspaper, I don't know. I served as a Standing Committee member in the Trotskyist faction. (Asked) Do you have any writings in the "Spark" publication? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) When did you meet Peng Shuzhi? (Answered) A long time ago, around 1922 or 1923. We met in Moscow. (Asked) Have you been to Japan? (Answered) I've been to Japan many times in the past. I studied in Japan, studying law, politics, and literature. I didn't graduate. (Asked) What did you go to Moscow for? (Answered) To take a look. I stayed for a month and then came back. (Asked) Where is the headquarters of the Trotskyist faction located? (Answered) This is an internal party matter; I don't want to say more. Please ask me about matters within the scope of the indictment. (Asked) Does the Third International provide you with assistance? (Answered) The Third International is the Stalinist faction and has no relationship with us. (Asked) Are there many people in your faction? (Answered) Our organization exists throughout the country, but we don't have many members, and our power is small. More workers participate, followed by students. In rural areas, we don't yet have the power to enter. (Asked) Roughly how many places are there in your party? (Asked) Do they join because they believe in the ideology? (Answered) Of course, otherwise, they wouldn't come to join. (Asked) Where does your financial support come from? (Answered) We raise it ourselves. Teachers contribute a portion of their salary, and workers contribute a portion of their wages. The amounts vary. (Asked) Do both the "Spark" and "School Life" publications contain your writings? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) Do you use the pseudonym "Li" in the concessions? (Answered) Of course, otherwise, I would have been arrested long ago. (Asked) Is Peng Shuzhi in the same organization as you? (Answered) Yes, he's also a Standing Committee member. He and I were expelled at the same time. (Asked) How many Standing Committee members are there in total? (Answered) Three official and two alternate. (Asked) Who are the alternate Standing Committee members? (Answered) Pu Yifang and Luo Shifan. I would like to take this opportunity to clarify that I did not read the records during the previous preliminary hearing. Today, the prosecutor mentioned in the indictment that Pu Yifan and Song Fengchun are alternate Standing Committee members, which is very strange. Song Fengchun is not an alternate Standing Committee member because, first, Song Fengchun was only released from prison when he was arrested. How could he be a Standing Committee member while in prison? Furthermore, any party has an odd number of Standing Committee members, either five or seven. If he were a Standing Committee member, there would be six people, which is absolutely impossible. Also, our alternate Standing Committee member, Pu Yifang, is from Sichuan, over thirty years old, and has a very dark complexion, not at all good-looking. But the one I saw today is a young child with a fair and beautiful face, not our Pu Yifang. (Asked) Peng Shuzhi once stated that the alternate Standing Committee members were Pu Yifan and Song Fengchun? (Answered) I don't know what he said, but according to my knowledge, it's not true. (At this point, lawyer Zhang Shizhao requested that the preliminary hearing records be given to Chen to read, and Chen also requested to see the documents. The judge gave Chen a package containing the "Spark" and "School Life" publications for detailed review. After about twenty minutes, Chen acknowledged that they were their publications.) (Asked) Is your claim that a Soviet government should be established first, and then the Red Army should be organized? (Answered) Yes. The Red Army is a military organization that should be based on the poor, peasants, and workers. (Asked) According to the current situation in China, do you think a Red Army is necessary? (Answered) The Red Army is just a name. I advocate the establishment of a peasant army. China's current situation is not about not writing about the Red Army, but organizing the Red Army according to the current situation is still impossible. (Asked) When will a Red Army be needed? (Answered) A Red Army is needed when there is political power, otherwise, the political power cannot be maintained. (Asked) What are your opinions on riots? (Answered) Revolutionary parties must riot to seize political power. The Nationalist Party's revolution was also a riot. (Asked) What do the three words "Soviet" mean? (Answered) It doesn't have any special meaning; it just means "meeting". (Asked) Should capitalists be overthrown? (Answered) Of course. (Asked) Do you advocate seizing political power? (Answered) Of course. What is a political party called if it doesn't want to seize political power? (Asked) Is labor-capital compromise right? (Answered) There is absolutely no possibility of labor-capital compromise. (Asked) Do you advocate organizing a proletarian government? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) Is there a publication called "Axe"? Is it yours? (Answered) Yes, it's distributed in North China. I'm not very clear who the editor is. I am the editor of "Spark." "School Life" is a publication from the South. (Asked) Is the Secretary the highest position? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) Do the "Red Bandits" in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui have anything to do with you? (Answered) No. (Asked) Do you participate? (Answered) Now is not the time for rioting. (At this point, the judge questioned in detail various important documents in the "Spark" and "School Life" publications to determine if they were written by Chen. Chen truthfully acknowledged each one. Among the main ones were: Opposing imperialism, developing the armed struggle of peasants and workers, opposing the Nationalist Party's two-line struggle, the current situation and tasks, accusing Japanese imperialists of invading Manchuria, resisting Japan to save the country, the Second Revolution, implementing the eight-hour system, publicizing military power, opposing the Emergency Criminal Law for Endangering the Republic of China, the situation after the League of Nations resolution, and a letter to comrades in the party about resisting Japan to save the country.) (Asked) What is the goal of the Trotskyist faction? (Answered) The biggest goal is world revolution, and the ultimate goal is the national liberation of China, opposing the military dictatorship system and seizing political power. (Asked) Do you advocate convening a national assembly with non-registered elections? (Answered) Yes. We have the right to convene this meeting if we have the power. The Nationalist Party has the right to convene it, and we will also participate. (Asked) Is it true that you cannot cooperate with the Red Bandits in Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Anhui, and Fujian due to differences in political views? (Answered) Yes. (Asked) Is your headquarters in Shanghai? (Answered) Yes, it's in my residence, on a very small scale. (Asked) Are your publications public? (Answered) Of course, we want them to be public; anyone can read them, but the government prohibits it, so everyone can't see them. Now, the judge finally has the opportunity to see them. (Asked) Do you often meet? (Answered) We meet often. (Asked) Were you arrested while meeting? (Answered) I was sick and didn't know. I've been sick for two months, but I used to participate in meetings. (Asked) Do you know about the many small notes found during the search? (Answered) I don't know. (Asked) Do you recognize all ten people who were arrested? (Answered) I recognize some, but not others. (Asked) Which ones do you recognize? (Answered) I cannot report on the internal affairs of the party. I can only talk about political opinions. It's the government's detectives' responsibility to determine who is a Communist. I cannot be a government detective. At this point, the judge asked Chen for the reasons for opposing the National Government. Chen listed three points and concluded by saying, "I admit that I oppose the National Government, but I do not admit that I endanger the Republic of China. I will present the reasons in detail during the debate." It was already 11:35 AM. The judge, considering that the interrogation was detailed enough, ordered Chen to leave the court and summoned Peng Shuzhi for interrogation.

Next, Peng Shuzhi is Summoned for Trial 92

(The judge asked) When did you join the Communist Party? (Peng answered) Around 1921. (Asked) What did you do before? (Answered) I studied in Hunan. After graduating, I taught at a higher primary school in Baoqing. Later, I joined the Communist Party. At that time, the Communist Party was not divided into factions. I was a CY (Communist Youth League member) and didn't do much work. (Asked) When did you meet Chen Duxiu? (Answered) In 1921 in Moscow. I studied at the Eastern University in Russia for four years. After graduating, I taught at that school. In 1924, I returned to China and edited publications such as "New Youth" in Shanghai and joined the Central Bureau. (Asked) Did you join Chen Duxiu's faction because you admired his writing? (Answered) There's no such thing as admiration or not. My advocacy for the liberation of China is the same as Chen Duxiu's. (Asked) When were you expelled from the Communist Party and why? (Answered) I was expelled at the same time as Chen Duxiu because of differences in political views. (Asked) Are you a Trotskyist? (Answered) Actually, it can't be called a Trotskyist faction. He's just a leader. (Asked) What exactly are the differences in your so-called political views? (Answered) It's hard to say. Generally speaking, I have different opinions on the attitude towards Soviet Russia and the proletarian movement system in Europe and China. (Asked) What is the foundation of the Communist Party? (Answered) Workers and peasants. As for the petty bourgeoisie, they often waver between the bourgeoisie and the proletariat. Relying on them for revolution is not feasible. (Asked) Is organizing an army necessary? (Answered) The dictatorship of the proletariat definitely needs a Red Army, but organizing a Red Army should be done after the victory of the proletarian revolution. Before the victory, only peasants can be armed. As for why China can produce such a large Red Army now, it is entirely due to objective conditions because the rural areas are bankrupt. (Asked) How many Trotskyists are there in Shanghai? (Answered) Our organization is promoting its doctrines and is not yet widespread. The strength is not great, and the number of people is not large. (Asked) Where does your funding come from? (Answered) We take it out of our own pockets. (Asked) Are you a Central Committee member? (Answered) Yes, I was elected at the same time as Chen Duxiu. The three Standing Committee members are Chen Duxiu, Zhang Jiwen (Note: this is a phonetic transcription), and me. The alternate Standing Committee members are Pu Yifang and Luo Shifan. (At this point, Peng again stated that he had not read the preliminary hearing records and proved that Pu Yifan and Song Fengchun were not alternate Central Committee members. Song was just a "party member." This is the same as what Chen Duxiu said. He also wrote down the names of Pu Yifang and Luo Shifan in handwriting and presented them to the court.) (Asked) Does the Third International provide you with any assistance? (Answered) No. (Asked) Did you edit the "Spark" and "School Life" publications? (Answered) Everything with my signature was done by me. (Asked) Do you oppose the National Government? (Answered) Of course, I oppose it. Otherwise, I wouldn't be here. (At this point, Peng Shuzhi stated three reasons for his opposition.) (Asked) Have you had any riots? (Answered) There were no riots. There was, of course, written propaganda. (At this point, it was already 12:30 PM. The judge then ordered him to leave the court and summoned Pu Yifan.)

Song and Two Others Cry Injustice 93

The judge then summoned Pu Yifan, who stated that he was 29 years old, from Huaining, Anhui, and resided at 322 Gaofuli, Mumuyuan Road, Shanghai. He had studied at Waseda University in Japan. After returning to China, he taught at a middle school in Anhui for a year and then went to Shanghai to engage in literary life. At the time of the arrest, he was the editor of a monthly magazine at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, with a monthly salary of 150 yuan. He didn't understand what an alternate Standing Committee member even was. At the time of the arrest, he was at Xie Shaoshan's house, but he didn't go there for a meeting; he went to find Zeng Zhaowei (Note: this is a phonetic transcription) because Li Weixia, the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, saw that my work was too hard and asked me to find a proofreader to copy. I went to Dongyouheng Road to find Zeng Zhaowei, but he wasn't there. Xie Shaoshan told me to wait a while. I don't know how I was arrested. The documents found in my residence were sent there by a friend. If they were mine, there would be no need to deny it. It's ridiculous that Xie Shaoshan said I was a committee member in the Second Branch of the High Court. How could I be a committee member if I'm not a Communist? After the arrest, the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company wanted to bail me out, but he himself had problems with another case. There were four people in the monthly magazine editorial department, and they were afraid of being implicated because of the Communist suspicion case, so of course they didn't dare to speak up. I am being wronged. Chen Duxiu once stated in the Second Branch of the High Court that he didn't know me; there are records to check. At this time, lawyer Hua Zuwang also stood up and stated that the box found in Pu's residence had another mark on it, which should be noted, and that many letters in the box had been discarded by the Western police, so the Western police who conducted the search should be summoned to testify. Pu also stated that the search was illegal, saying that they were hitting and bumping randomly and that he had asked the Western police to register the documents in the box, but they were not allowed to do so. It was 12:45 PM. The judge summoned Wang Wu (i.e., Song Fengchun), who stated that he was arrested on October 15th of last year in Chunyangli, Dongyouheng Road. I went to Xie Shaoshan to borrow money because I was released on bail from prison due to illness on October 5th and didn't have a single penny. Xie Shaoshan was a friend of mine from before. He agreed to lend me money, so I went with him, and I was arrested. I used to be a Trotskyist in the Communist Party, but after being released on bail on October 5th, Zhu had no actions. Saying that I am an alternate Central Committee member of the Communist Party, I cannot mix fish eyes with pearls. Please don't call a deer a horse in court either. It was 1:30 PM. The judge summoned the defendants and announced that the time was up for today and that the trial would continue at 9:00 AM tomorrow (the 15th).

Songjiang

The Magistrate Demolishes the Fence Built Around Yuecheng 94

Since the demolition of the west gate of this city, it has become a prosperous area. The former county party department had proposed building a Sun Yat-sen memorial monument on the Yuecheng site and sent a letter to the county government for handling. Later, due to the fact that a Mr. Wu had leased vacant land from the government property bureau at that location, if the memorial monument project were to proceed, it would hinder Mr. Wu's leased land and the buildings constructed. He repeatedly filed appeals with the provincial and county governments to revoke the county government's decision on the design plan and the method of allocating land sections for public use after acquiring private land. People from all walks of life also repeatedly petitioned the provincial and county governments to support the party department's proposal. Official documents were exchanged back and forth for three years, and the case piled up. Later, the provincial government ordered the civil affairs and construction departments to review and decide to move the Sun Yat-sen memorial monument to Zhongshan Park in Yuhuangge, while the original proposed site for the monument in Yuecheng was reserved for public construction and handled in accordance with the county government's land section allocation method to resolve the dispute. The provincial government immediately relayed the order to the county government for implementation. The former County Magistrate Shen announced the order. Unexpectedly, Mr. Wu hastily built a fence around the vacant land, and the current County Magistrate Jin also ordered the Public Security Bureau and the First District Office to protect it. After being warned by the bureau and office, Mr. Wu also wrote a petition to the county for instructions, which has now been approved. The approval stated that since the case has been determined by the provincial government, the county government can only strictly comply with it. The built fence should still be demolished immediately to facilitate allocation. It is said that County Magistrate Jin will actively handle the allocation of land sections to resolve the dispute and appease the public's expectations.

Wujiang

The County Government Sends Personnel to Supervise the Burning of Items Pawned at Tongren Pawnshop 95

The Tongren Pawnshop, originally located in Chefangzhen, Wu County, suffered significant losses due to robbery. It moved to Tonglizhen in this county last year to operate. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 12th, a sudden fire broke out, completely destroying all the silver, jewelry, and storage rooms. The Second District Office reported the incident to the county government for on-site inspection to determine the actual situation. The county government has now ordered the County Chamber of Commerce, the Second District Chief, and the Chief of the Second Public Security Branch to jointly supervise the pawnshop, collect the pawned goods, and submit a list to the county for verification to clarify the truth.

Wuxi

Deliberating on Rescuing the Silk Industry 96

Cai Pei, the Administrative Inspector of the Second District, stated that Wuxi and Wujin counties under his jurisdiction are known as special silk areas in Jiangsu Province for their prosperity and development. Recently, affected by the social economy, farmers' livelihoods have been exhausted, and it is difficult to maintain their operations. Now that the silkworm season is approaching, it is imperative to rescue the silkworm breeding industry. He has formulated rescue measures, which are divided into two main points: (1) Farmers' silkworm breeding capital should be provided with low-interest loans to complete their operational strength. (2) The price of spring cocoons in this period should be considered in advance, and a maximum price should be determined and announced to farmers to arouse their interest. The above measures have been telegraphed to each county yesterday, summoning the responsible representatives of the relevant industries to quickly implement the measures to revitalize people's livelihoods and save the industry.

Jiangyin

County Magistrate Ruan Inspects the Chengwu Road 97

The reconstruction project of the Zhencheng Road and Chengwu Road, the section from Xiwai to Xishiqiao, has been gradually completed. On the 13th, County Magistrate Ruan and acting technical director Yang Pinsun inspected the western countryside and also inspected the Xiagang River project. County Magistrate Ruan found that the roadbed of the Chengwu section had several projects that were quite simple and crude, with the roadbed and the field base indistinguishable in height. If it rained, the roadbed would be destroyed. He immediately ordered the village chiefs to persuade the working farmers to build the roadbed firmly and to take the soil from the ditches on both sides to achieve a permanent solution. This inspection ended at Xishiqiao, and they returned to the city that night.

Yangzhou

Local Budget Increased by 100,000 Yuan 98

The local budget of Jiangdu County for the 21st year was 500,000 yuan. Now that County Magistrate Ma, concurrently holding the position, has been ordered by the provincial government to prepare the local budget for the 22nd year, he ordered his subordinates to complete the compilation. Compared with the previous year, it has increased by about 100,000 yuan, designated to be drawn from the land tax. It is reported that the provincial government is awaiting instructions.

The son of a farmer, Guo Yougong, in Wangguan Town, the fifth district of the county, was kidnapped by bandits last month, and there was no news of him. Returning the Sheng Family's Fields and Properties 101

Sheng Xuanhuai (Xingsun) of the late Qing Dynasty had many estates in Jiangsu, such as the Liuyuan on Wufu Road, the property of the Datong Hotel on Chuangma Road, and the ancestral fields and houses, worth more than 500,000 yuan. In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the Executive Yuan ordered the county to seal them all and the county government sent personnel to manage them. The Wu County government received an order from the Executive Yuan yesterday to clear all of them and return them to the Sheng family for management. It is also reported that the Sheng family's properties in Changzhou, Wuxi, Hangzhou, and other places will also be returned to the Sheng family.

Bandits Rob a Farmer's Family and Shoot the Head of the Household 102

In Chuanshan Village, about two miles away from Shishen in the southern countryside of Huzhou, there is a farmer named Shen Yatou, whose family is well-off, which led to bandits coveting their property. Around midnight the day before yesterday, two bandit ships suddenly arrived, carrying more than twenty bandits, each armed with guns and speaking in a Hakka accent. They broke into the house, overturning boxes and cabinets, and carried out a large-scale search, looting cotton, silk clothes, silk, jewelry, etc., with losses of about 200 yuan. Shen Yatou was shot in the leg by the bandits, and his son, Liushun, was injured in the face. Afterward, the family sent them to the Kuihu Police Hospital for treatment.

On the afternoon of the 13th, several soldiers from the artillery battalion of Liu Zhennian's army went to the nearby Hutou Chen area to capture chickens and ducks in the countryside, which led to the villagers ringing gongs and gathering a crowd to take them back, which aroused the soldiers' anger. Illegally Stealing Bamboo Shoots Leads to a Fatal Case 104

Qidu in the southern countryside of Xiaoshan is known for producing bamboo shoots. This year, the output is limited, which has led to an increase in prices, and many poor households often steal them privately, so the mountain owners all hate it. On the morning of the 14th, someone secretly stole from a bamboo shoot garden owned by the Gu family. They suspected that the neighbor, the Shen family, had done it. They searched the Shen family's house at that time, and they quarreled with each other. The Gu family and the Shen family immediately fought. As a result, two members of the Shen family were killed. Seeing that they had caused a disaster, the Gu family immediately asked the gentry to come forward to mediate, and then compensated for the matter.

New President of the Central Bank, Kong Xiangxi, Assumed Office Yesterday 107

The Central Government Dispatched Cai Yuanpei to Deliver an Instructive Address

Mr. Kong Xiangxi, the newly appointed President of the Central Bank, held his official oath ceremony in the bank's auditorium at 9:00 AM yesterday.
