Cai Yuanpei, representing the Central Party Headquarters, and Song Ziwen, representing the Executive Yuan, delivered instructive addresses. All bank staff attended and participated. After Mr. Kong delivered his reply, the ceremony concluded at 10:00 AM. The details are recorded as follows:

Ceremony Order 108

(1) Everyone stand at attention; (2) Bow three times to the Party and National Flag and the Founder's Will; (3) The President respectfully reads the Founder's Will; (4) Observe three minutes of silence; (5) The President takes the oath; (6) The representative of the National Government presents the seal of office; (7) The representative of the Central Party Headquarters delivers an instructive address; (8) The representative of the National Government delivers an instructive address; (9) The representative of the Executive Yuan delivers an instructive address; (10) The President delivers a reply; (11) Ceremony concludes; (12) Photograph.

Kong's Oath 109

After the ceremony proceeded as scheduled, the new President, Kong Xiangxi, raised his left hand and read the oath aloud. The oath stated: "I solemnly swear that I will恪遵 (kè zūn - respectfully obey) the Founder's Will, obey the Party, abide by national laws, be loyal and diligent in my duties, and economize on expenses. I will never employ useless personnel, engage in corruption, or accept bribes. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment from the Party."

Cai's Instructive Address 110

Cai Yuanpei, representing the Central Party Headquarters, delivered an instructive address, stating: "Today, former Minister Kong has been ordered to assume the position of President of the Central Bank.

Kong Xiangxi (left), President, and Song Ziwen (right), Minister, taking a photo together (photographed by Li Zunyong)

The Central Bank is a national bank, and its mission is different from other banks. It is of great importance to the future of the country. Under the current circumstances, its major missions are approximately three-fold: (1) To relieve and revitalize the rural areas. Our country's rural economy is already in a state of bankruptcy. It is hoped that President Kong will use the power of the nation's financial center to find ways to provide relief and seek the revitalization of the rural areas; (2) To promote domestic goods. Our country's domestic goods still cannot compete with foreign goods, resulting in foreign goods flooding the market, capital outflow, and the decline of industry and commerce. An important reason is the limitation of capital. It is hoped that the financial sector will find ways to support the development of industry and commerce; (3) To reform the currency. The government has issued a clear order to unify the currency, abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan. In its initial stage, the national currency has not yet become uniform. The Central Bank is responsible for regulating the national finance and supplying hard currency. It is hoped that the mission of currency unification can be completed in a short period of time. The Central Bank was founded by Minister Song. In the past, the results have been excellent. As for various plans that have not been implemented, it is hoped that Comrade Kong will continue to implement them. The future of the country depends on this. The Party has great expectations."

Song's Address 111

Finance Minister Song Ziwen delivered an instructive address, stating: "Today, I represent the National Government and the Executive Yuan. In my capacity as former President, I will briefly offer my humble opinions and bid farewell to all the comrades of the Central Bank. The establishment of the Central Bank was the dying wish of our late Founder. Therefore, the steps taken were not overly hasty, but proceeded step by step, hoping to consolidate the foundation. Therefore, in recent years, despite repeated floods, internal unrest, and foreign aggression, the Central Bank has been able to stand firm. This is due to this approach. As for all the internal affairs of the Central Bank, everything is open and transparent, because the credit of a national bank is the credit of the nation. Therefore, the candidates for supervisors and directors of this bank are mostly famous figures in society. I recall that when dealing with the Hankou flood two years ago, the government, in response to the actual needs, established a flood relief committee. The public initially had doubts but later became convinced. Similarly, in the past, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company repeatedly dispatched high-ranking officials to reorganize it due to the poor performance of its managers, but to no avail. However, this is not the case now. My resignation from the presidency of the Central Bank has caused external doubts, which are actually inaccurate. In fact, I resigned because the Central Bank is gradually developing, and its affairs are numerous, and I cannot take care of both. Therefore, Mr. Kong will succeed me. Mr. Kong has been involved in practical industries and has new ideas and the courage to take action, so he will definitely be able to take on the job. I am here to say goodbye to my colleagues at the Central Bank. I hope that my colleagues at the Central Bank will love Mr. Kong as they love Ziwen, so that the future of the Central Bank can become increasingly prosperous."

Kong's Reply 112

President Kong Xiangxi replied, stating: "This time, I have been ordered to assume the position of President of the Central Bank. I believe that the President's position is of great importance to the nation's finance, and because of my ill health, I had expressed my unwillingness to take on the job. Because the Central Bank was founded single-handedly by Minister Song and has a close relationship with the nation's finances, Minister Song should continue to serve during this time of national crisis. Later, I was repeatedly urged by my comrades in the Central Government to take office in order to express the spirit of overcoming national difficulties together. Now, in response to Mr. Cai's instructive address, I hope to achieve the main points of the Central Bank and to complete the mission of the Central Bank, as reported by Minister Song. I will certainly abide by this. In the early days of preparing the Central Bank in Guangdong, I received a handwritten order from the Founder and allocated 3,000 yuan, ordering Minister Song to prepare. At that time, Guangdong was occupied by warlords. Minister Song used a spirit of adventure to borrow money to print banknotes from the American Bank Note Company. I once served as the Minister of Industry, Acting Minister of Finance, and President of the Central Bank in Guangdong, but neither the Guangdong Central Bank nor the Hankou Central Bank were consolidated and could not achieve the purpose of their establishment. The third Shanghai Central Bank has reached today's position through Minister Song's painstaking planning. Its domestic credit is remarkable, and its foreign reputation is excellent. The Central Bank is the nation's financial institution, like the blood vessels of the human body. If the financial circulation of a country is smooth, it can enrich the country and strengthen the people. As for how to develop China's economy, how to relieve farmers, and how to revitalize industry, the first step should be (1) to consolidate the foundation of the Central Bank, (2) to develop step by step, and (3) to lead the financial sector to embrace a spirit of unity and cooperation, in order to achieve the goal. Now, under the guidance and assistance of experienced directors and supervisors, I will continue the policies of former President Song and work hard to implement them step by step in order to meet the hopes of all sectors."

Separate Instructions 113

After assuming office, President Kong Xiangxi separately convened senior bank officials in the President's office to give instructions and encourage them. At the same time, he received Chinese and foreign guests who came to congratulate him. Mr. Kong said that he did not bring a single personal assistant with him this time, and there were no changes to the entire staff. Many gifts were presented to President Kong by various sectors, all of which were displayed in the President's office.

The total length of the coastline is more than 12,000 li, and fish, shellfish, and algae are abundant. Few countries in the world can compare. To the south, there are warm currents passing through the South China Sea and the East China Sea. To the north, there are cold currents affecting the Bohai Sea and the Yellow Sea. It is difficult to get a general idea without several years of hard work.

Invasion Ambition Japan's policy of aggression against me has two parts, one is the continental policy of the north, and the other is the marine policy of the south. The former takes the army as the backing, the South Manchuria Railway as the guide, and the occupation of the Northeast as the purpose. The latter takes the navy as the backing, the fishing and shipping industries as the guide, and the occupation of coastal provinces and inland rivers in the interior as the purpose. From an economic point of view, the southern marine aggression policy is more noteworthy for people's livelihood and national defense. The Japanese invasion of fishing in the coastal areas of Jiangsu Province began to show traces at the beginning of the year. Before this, as the former Commercial and Ministry of Commerce Shi Pi and current researcher of the Shimonoseki Joint Aquatic Products Co., Ltd., Kumatato Shiro, inspected the fishing industry in my country's coastal areas every year, dividing it into spring and autumn. Another example is that the Japanese Kishigami Ryukichi, who died of illness in Sichuan a few years ago, was a professor at the Japanese Empire University and was also a special commissioner to investigate the Yangtze River aquatic products business. Secondly, such as the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, the Tokyo Fisheries Training Institute, and the survey and internship ships of the aquatic product test sites in various prefectures and counties also come to my country's coastal areas from time to time, using the survey results to guide their country's fishing industry. Its plan can be said to have obtained Dalian as the root of the North Sea region, Qingdao and the southwestern part of Japan as the base of the Yellow Sea region, and Taiwan as the base of the East China Sea and the South China Sea. There are already many fixed fishing grounds in the Dalian area. In the Qingdao area, the salt fields near Jiaozhou are all in their grasp. However, in Shanghai, there are more people in my country who operate aquatic businesses, and the talents are also more concentrated, making it difficult to get started. Therefore, it is planned to do its best to build a tight fishing wall in Shanghai within a few years. It has been heard that the Japanese government is dispatching guidance personnel in Shanghai. For example, Japanese fishing boats are imported on schedule, and fishing is carried out arbitrarily in nearby seas, all of which are planned and organized. My oppression is also. In addition, in recent years, the Japanese government has encouraged the army and navy to study the fishing industry, and aquatic personnel to complete their studies in the army and navy. The facts are scattered in various magazines and are no longer rare. In the Yuan and Ming dynasties, Japanese pirates ran rampant in coastal areas, and they thought it was the most glorious, and the lower Japanese fishing boats have reached more than 30,000. The problems in my country's economic, people's livelihood, and national defense are also serious.

The situation is becoming more urgent The Japanese side is vigorously implementing its marine aggression policy, as described above. Recently, it has become more and more urgent. For example, last year's No. 85 Fudokyu and more than 20 other ships carried out indiscriminate harvesting in the fishing grounds of Huadao Mountain and Shengshan. On one side, the Japanese government commissioned Hirata Yasada, director of the Yokohama Aquarium, to come to Shanghai, using the name of establishing an aquarium to continue the shore-based investigation. In May of the 19th year, the Navy dispatched more than a thousand fishing boats led by warships, and spread them outside Lin Hongkou to fish freely. If they encountered my country's fishing boats, they would arbitrarily invade them and use violence to prevent them. Later, the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry held the so-called fisheries conference, and the attendees were important figures in the country's aquatic products industry. The resolutions directly affected the development of my country's fishing industry. Those who are indirectly related to my rights and national defense are very large. After that, eight Japanese sea-operated net trawlers, etc., were named cargo ships carrying ice and fresh goods to Shanghai for dumping. All of these were explicit actions. Recently, there are many Japanese foreign firms in Shanghai, all of which are responsible for promoting and assisting the aquatic products business run by the Japanese. In addition, the number of Japanese ice and fresh goods imported from Dalian and Qingdao is also increasing day by day. Two years ago, more than 30 Japanese fishing boats were imported on schedule. Recently, fresh yellow croaker directly sent and sold by the Japanese was found in the 16th Pier fish market in Shanghai. I am grateful for your association's telegram to all the generals in the country to be my support. The good news has been transmitted, and the entire army is encouraged. I will continue to work hard and desperately kill the enemy in order to live up to the expectations of the people of the whole country. Although my army is ordered to move its defense area, the positions protruding from Fengning Guojiatun and other areas have been under siege by the enemy for ten days, and there has not been a day without a deadly battle with the enemy. This battle situation is also only told to the people of the whole country. I am here to reply to you. Please inspect it. Army Commander of the 41st Army, Sun Kuiyuan, and all officers and soldiers kowtow together. Yang Yin.

Recent Tea Industry Improvement and Inspection Guidelines The Commodity Inspection Bureau Expresses Its Views 122

In recent years, my country's tea exports have decreased year by year, which has a great impact on the finances and rural economy of various parts of my country. Yesterday, reporters from various newspapers visited Cai Wuji, Director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, and inquired about the recent tea industry reform and inspection methods. He gave detailed opinions, which are recorded as follows: (The following are Director Cai's opinions)

There are many reasons for the failure of my country's tea industry. The most important ones are that the cultivation and manufacturing methods are too old, and the complex procedures of green tea coloring and tea merchant transactions are also one aspect. Since the bureau started the tea silk import inspection in July of the previous year, in addition to the routine inspection work, the investigation of the tea situation (research is also spared no effort. At the same time, it is recognized that the improvement of cultivation and manufacturing methods is the most important and urgent task at present. Therefore, on the one hand, it is linked to the Hunan Provincial Tea Affairs Experiment Site and the Anhui Provincial Tea Industry Improvement Site, which are responsible for the red and green tea conversion work. , and jointly leased the original site of the Bai Yekeng Zhenzhi Tea Farm in Jiangnan Xiushui, preparing to set up a jointly run tea industry improvement farm. On the one hand, it commissioned mechanical experts to create and improve several red and green tea improvement machines, preparing to divide the methods of red tea withering, fermenting, drying, and fate tea steaming, carving, frying, and rolling into small-scale farmer production equipment and large-scale factory equipment, entrusting them to each improvement farm for separate trials. Although this year is the first phase of trials, it should be able to open up a new path in the tea manufacturing field, so as to greet the private sector, actively transform, and China's tea gardens are all small-scale sideline production. In recent years, due to the sluggish exports, the trees have become old and the mountains have become desolate.

The tea quality has also become inferior due to this. I have also entrusted various improved agencies to engage in the trial voting of tea tree varieties to create new varieties. At a minimum, the tea garden varieties must be pure. It is also planned to try planting Indian and Ceylon tea varieties for comparison. In addition, such items as pruning, fertilizing, and cultivating are also closely related to tea quality and cost, and are also being actively tested. As for the bureau's inspection policy, in the past, only the minimum tea standard and several items such as moisture and ash were set. Since the new tea was launched this year, measures have also been added to crack down on colored tea. The purpose of this item is to crack down on tea leaves with excessive coloring. The bureau has samples available and will distribute them to various tea shops for reference in the future. In addition, it is necessary to prohibit the export of yellow aluminum chromate (commonly known as light yellow), Sanyu Huang Yiji Huang, green arsenic steel gasified copper (commonly known as sand green, etc.) and other toxic coloring materials. If so, the coloring materials that have damaged the tea quality in the past can be gradually reduced, and foreigners can also be prevented from saying that Chinese tea contains harmful substances, making unfavorable publicity for me in various countries. In addition, the set moisture standard is the best way to eliminate the sale of wet tea. In the past, there were many unqualified teas due to slightly higher moisture content. Now, tea merchants in various places are purchasing raw tea and starting to bake it. It is also hoped that they will automatically and strictly crack down on wet tea and add baking to prevent the excellent quality from deteriorating due to moisture. The above-mentioned crackdown measures were decided by the inspection technology conference convened by the Ministry of Industry last month, and will soon be announced by the Ministry of Industry. The bureau can immediately forward it to the Chinese and foreign tea merchants, he said.

Statement from Director Xu of the Public Works Bureau Regarding the Signing of the Provisional Telephone Contract 123

Regarding the signing of the provisional telephone contract, recent news has been inconsistent, attracting considerable attention from various quarters. Yesterday, newspapers published the draft contract, stating that it had been approved by the Ministry of Transportation and that the approval order arrived in Shanghai on the 13th. It was also reported that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Company had agreed to formally sign the contract on the 18th of this month. Reporters, recognizing the importance of this matter, visited Director Xu Peihuang of the Municipal Public Works Bureau to inquire about the truth. According to Director Xu, the Public Works Bureau had long since submitted the draft provisional contract to the Municipal Government for record. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau had also submitted it to the Ministry of Transportation, and the Shanghai Telephone Company had obtained the consent of the authorities of the two concessions. All procedures were ready, and the contract could have been signed earlier. However, the Shanghai Telephone Company had not yet received written permission from the two concessions. More recently, due to stipulations in the contract and related regulations regarding fees payable to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, the contract specified "full rental fees and half of the rental fees," without determining the exact amounts. The Shanghai Telephone Company, when negotiating with the two concession authorities, had already declared its fees based on the Shanghai Telephone Bureau's current rental rates. Therefore, without specifying the exact amounts and only stipulating "rental fees and half," they feared future disputes. Consequently, they requested the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to confirm the exact amounts in writing to avoid conflicts. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau recently sought instructions from the Ministry of Transportation regarding this matter. Today's newspaper report that the contract has been approved by the Ministry of Transportation likely refers to this issue and does not mean that the contract itself was only recently approved. Currently, the company has received written permission from the two concession authorities. Once the Shanghai Telephone Bureau delivers the written confirmation of the rental fee amounts to the Shanghai Telephone Company, a signing date can be set. It is expected to occur within the next few days. However, the newspaper report that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Company have agreed to formally sign the contract on the 18th of this month is not accurate. This provisional contract is to be signed by the Public Works Bureau, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, and the Shanghai Telephone Company. Therefore, the official signing date should be agreed upon by all three parties. Furthermore, the date of publication of the original contract should also be determined jointly by the three signing parties after the formal signing to ensure due solemnity. The newspaper report that the contract will be officially announced immediately after signing is also inaccurate. Director Xu of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has stated that he will issue a correction regarding all the inaccuracies reported in the news.

Feng Bingnan Explains Transitional Measures in Water Fee Dispute 124

Two letters, one from Kui Yanfang, chairman of the Shanghai Real Estate Association, and one from mediator Feng Bingnan, concerning the water issue are of great importance. The original texts are reproduced below:

Letter to Feng Bingnan: Respected Mr. Bingnan, this water dispute is not only related to public health but also affects the lives of users. Our association, as a collective of industries entrusted by the public, has exhausted its efforts but failed to resolve it. Fortunately, your sense of public duty and willingness to mediate have gradually brought the matter within scope, and the temporary transitional measures to resolve the dispute take all aspects into consideration. Not only will all users benefit greatly, but all responsible parties will also be indebted to you. However, the newspaper reports regarding these transitional measures and the trial period, as well as the organization of the advisory committee, are not detailed enough. Therefore, we send this special letter to express our gratitude to you on behalf of all users. We also respectfully request that you provide a detailed explanation of the trial measures so that we can study them and inform the public. We apologize for troubling you and eagerly await your reply. With respectful wishes for your well-being.

Reply to Kui Yanfang: In response to your letter of the 5th of this month, I have carefully reviewed its contents and am grateful for your kind words, which I do not deserve. This water dispute has been ongoing for years without resolution. I, in my ignorance, initially paid no attention to this matter and did not wish to make any suggestions. However, both you and Mr. Hu Jun'an expressed that the dispute was intensifying, that misunderstandings between parties were increasing, and that the delay was causing considerable harm to the citizens. You both requested that I step in to mediate. Recognizing that this matter concerned the livelihood of the people, I agreed to participate in discussions as an independent party, without favoring any side. I also believed that all matters should be discussed face-to-face to avoid misunderstandings. Based on this principle, I proposed that the Public Works Bureau, the Shanghai Waterworks Company, and your association each appoint representatives to discuss the matter together. This proposal was accepted by all parties. As a result of the meetings, your association presented a statement, and the Shanghai Waterworks Company presented a table of water price tiers for study. I believed that controlling water wastage was the key to resolving this matter and that whether there was wastage should be determined by whether the necessary water consumption was exceeded. Therefore, I proposed a compromise, stipulating a trial period to estimate the necessary water consumption for each user. If this amount was exceeded, the water fees would be calculated based on the value of the property. During my participation in the discussions and mediation, I was deeply gratified that the members of your association maintained a broad perspective, patiently awaiting a resolution, and did not create further disputes. Now that the proposed trial measures are about to be implemented, I sincerely hope that all members of your association, as well as all citizens, will work together with the Public Works Bureau and the Waterworks Company to control water wastage and reduce the burden of water fees for the citizens. "Wastage" refers to consumption exceeding the necessary amount. Users only need water for drinking and cleaning purposes, and these purposes do not require wastage. If all users understand this and completely eliminate water wastage, the reduction in water fees will be considerable. Regarding the points you inquired about in your letter, in addition to what has already been explained above, I provide further point-by-point answers for clarity: (1) The current proposed water price is for a certain amount of water, which is based on the current total water meter readings in other houses and then increased by a substantial amount to determine the necessary water consumption. (2) The newly proposed water price table is sufficient to meet the needs of users for good hygiene, and the water price calculation does not exceed 75% of the property value. If the above water consumption is exceeded, additional water fees will be charged for the extra water. The method for calculating these extra water fees will vary based on the property level. For houses with the lowest rent, the price is 1.71 hao per thousand gallons; for houses with the highest rent, the price is 7.5 li per thousand gallons. (3) Water fees are calculated based on rent. The categorization has already been listed in the table, which is attached. (4) The new water price table has been approved by the Public Works Bureau. Although its effective period has not been specified, during this trial period, a more accurate statistic of the necessary water consumption for household use should be obtained. In addition, the Waterworks Company has two more points that I was previously asked to convey to your association: (1) The company is willing to do its best to assist the members of your association in controlling water wastage. (2) The company derives no benefit from the renewal contract with the Public Works Bureau for the universal installation of water meters. It is only seeking to benefit all citizens of the concession. This letter is sent in reply, hoping for your attention. The water fee calculation table is listed below:

Chamber of Commerce Explains Silver Coin Names After Implementation of the Abolition of the Tael System 126

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on a letter from the Insurance Association, requested clarification on the names of silver coins after the abolition of the tael system to ensure uniformity. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce immediately provided an interpretation based on the laws, stating that the term "silver coin" should be used. The correspondence is recorded below:

Letter from the Insurance Association 127

Dear Sirs, We received your letter of March 17, stating that according to the Ministry's order, all account books, contracts, and newly issued loans should uniformly use the silver coin standard from the date of the order, and the use of silver taels is no longer permitted. We have notified our colleagues to comply accordingly. However, although this matter is now universally implemented in the market, the name of the silver coin has not yet been clearly stipulated by the Ministry's order. Whether the name "silver coin" will be officially adopted in the future, or whether names such as "national currency," "silver dollar," or "silver ocean" can still be used according to previous custom, and whether they can be used arbitrarily, all require clarification. At the beginning of this currency system reform, if a consistent name is not specified, there will be inconveniences in the future, as the names used in the account books and contracts of various industries will differ. In view of the foregoing, we respectfully request that your association submit this matter for discussion and determine a standard name for universal use in all industries. We eagerly await your decision. Addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Reply from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 128

We received your letter regarding the name after the abolition of the tael system, whether the name "silver coin" should be officially adopted, or whether names such as "national currency," "silver dollar," or "silver ocean" can still be used, and requesting a discussion to determine a standard name. The term "national currency" refers to currency other than foreign currency, and its types include silver, copper, silver dollars, and silver oceans. These two terms are also used without consideration. Considering the need for a unified name, the decision should be limited to terms that are legally based. The recently promulgated Silver Standard Coinage Regulations by the government refer to the existing one-dollar silver coin as simply "silver coin," and the new silver coin to be minted is called "silver standard coin." Therefore, the term "silver coin" has become a legal name. Your association may notify your colleagues to uniformly change the name to "silver coin" to achieve consistency. We hope you will consider this. Addressed to the Shanghai Insurance Association.

Five Provinces and Cities Transportation Commission Revises Regulations on Interprovincial Highway Transportation 129

Article 19 of the Five Provinces and Cities Interprovincial Highway Transportation Regulations has now been revised and promulgated as follows: (1) The Transportation Commissions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Nanjing, and Shanghai Municipality have specially formulated these Interprovincial Highway Transportation Regulations to improve travel convenience. (2) The starting and ending stations for interprovincial highway transportation within the five provinces and cities shall be determined through consultations among the relevant interprovincial transportation organizations. The locations for changing vehicles shall not be limited to county or provincial boundaries and should be suitable locations in the reached cities and towns. (3) The frequency of interprovincial transportation and the departure times shall be jointly determined by the interprovincial transportation organizations of each province and city. (4) The fare table for interprovincial passengers and luggage shall be determined by mutual agreement based on the regulations of each route. If any party makes changes, the other party must be notified in advance for consultation and revision. (5) The number of interprovincial passengers and the volume of luggage shall be mutually notified by the departure station to other interprovincial stations via telephone to facilitate vehicle preparation. (6) The formats of interprovincial passenger tickets, luggage tickets, and other forms and advertisements required for interprovincial transportation shall be drafted and distributed by the respective interprovincial transportation organizations, and the costs shall be borne separately by each party. (7) The total amount of revenue from interprovincial transportation shall be mutually reported by each interprovincial transportation organization every ten days. All ticket revenue must be settled monthly, and by the 10th of each month, the various monthly report forms (interprovincial revenue statements, luggage statements, etc.) shall be exchanged along with the collected canceled passenger tickets and luggage tickets for verification. Settlement statements must be prepared and delivered by the 20th of the same month. (8) If passengers lose their interprovincial passenger tickets en route, the regulations for replacing tickets of the interprovincial transportation organizations of each province and city shall be followed. (9) If passengers who have purchased interprovincial tickets encounter special circumstances that prevent them from departing, they shall explain the reasons to the ticket station. The ticket may be refunded only after the station manager's permission. However, if a passenger requests to cancel the trip en route, the unused interprovincial tickets will not be refunded. (10) The interprovincial transportation vehicle shall be filled out by each interprovincial transportation station with a list of luggage received and delivered, and after separate verification and signing, the luggage shall be transported to the arrival station. (11) If interprovincial luggage is lost, compensation shall be paid by the party responsible for the loss in accordance with the regulations. However, no liability shall be assumed for losses caused by natural disasters or special circumstances that cannot be averted by human effort. (12) Upon arrival at the destination station, interprovincial luggage shall be delivered upon presentation of the luggage ticket. If the luggage ticket is lost, the station manager should be notified immediately, and a sufficient guarantee should be provided to receive the luggage. Otherwise, the interprovincial transportation organization shall not be liable if the luggage is claimed by another person. (13) Interprovincial passengers shall comply with the boarding regulations established by the interprovincial transportation organizations of each province and city. (14) Interprovincial passengers under 1.25 meters in height shall be charged half fare. Passengers held in the hands and not occupying a seat shall be exempt from fares. (15) Concessionary tickets for military police shall not be sold for interprovincial passenger tickets. (16) Matters concerning interprovincial transportation disputes shall be handled by the governments of the respective provinces and cities within their respective territories. Matters involving two or more provinces and cities shall be mediated by this commission. (17) If the regulations of each province and city on the interprovincial transportation route conflict with these regulations, these regulations shall prevail. (18) These regulations may be revised by this commission if there are any matters not covered. (19) These regulations shall be circulated by the National Economic Commission to the governments of each province and city for reference and implementation after being approved by the Transportation Commission of the Five Provinces and Cities.

Business Suspension of Bicycle Shops in the French Concession Yesterday: Report 132

Rules for Business Suspension Established at Yesterday's Meeting

Notice to All Businesses for Compliance

The report about the wind of business suspension arising among all bicycle shops in the French Concession to protest against the harsh taxes levied by the French Municipal Council has been recorded in previous newspapers. The following are the news from yesterday, divided and recorded as follows:

Rules for Business Suspension Established 133

The French Concession All Bicycle Shop Joint Office established eight rules for business suspension yesterday and notified all businesses to comply with them. The notice is recorded below: For the matter of notification, the French Municipal Council has illegally levied harsh taxes and exercised oppressive measures by suspending water and electricity supply. In order to cope with this, our businesses convened a meeting and decided to organize this office, appoint eleven representatives to be responsible for negotiations, and establish a joint volunteer letter as follows: 1. All businesses unanimously insist to the end and vow to reject the special tax and must not pay it privately. 2. Jointly abide by the resolution, consistently, and must not violate it. 3. Must not privately open for business until a complete solution is obtained. 4. All external and internal affairs must not be acted upon privately. If there are opinions, they can be reported to the representatives and submitted for public discussion and implementation. 5. All negotiation expenses shall be shared jointly by all and must not be shirked. 6. There must be no withdrawal midway or undermining of unity. 7. If any business is sued for resisting the tax or arrested by the patrol, mutual assistance should be provided and must not be shirked to show unity. 8. If any of the above articles are violated, all losses suffered and all negotiation expenses and donations incurred by all businesses due to this opposition to the tax shall be borne by the violator as a punishment. The above eight articles shall be signed and sealed by all businesses for joint compliance. It is hoped that all businesses will persist to the end in the future, and this office will be responsible for negotiations in accordance with the resolution of the General Assembly. Please note and wait patiently for a solution. Sincerely, Shanghai City Bicycle Repair Industry Association.

Chinese Workers Dismissed from American Merchant Ships Seek Severance Pay 136

Chinese Seamen Account for 80% of Dismissals

Organize Appeal to the Maritime Party Branch for Assistance

American merchant shipping companies, including the United States Mail Steamship Company, etc., had previously dismissed all their Chinese seamen in order to rescue and maintain the lives of American workers, as the government ordered, due to the increasing number of unemployed American workers in the midst of the global economic panic. Therefore, after receiving the order, the companies have successively dismissed Chinese workers starting this year, accounting for 80% of the total. It is now known that the dismissed workers believe that there is no reason for the dismissal, so they have jointly reported to the Seamen's Union, which has forwarded the request to the Special Maritime Party Branch of China for assistance. At the same time, they have organized the "Appeal Association of Dismissed Chinese Workers from American Merchant Ships" to unite and discuss countermeasures. It is said that what the association is asking for is that each dismissed worker should be given considerable severance pay by the company, depending on the number of years of service, to provide funds for seeking other jobs. They do not hope to be reinstated, as they know that the dismissal of Chinese workers by the company was ordered by the government, and it is impossible to reverse the situation.

Settlement of the Labor Dispute at Ewo Cotton Mill 137

Yesterday Morning, Party and Government Organs Convened Both Parties for Mediation

The Velvet and Silk Waste Departments Shut Down; Workers Receive Travel Expenses to Return Home

Recently, the velvet and silk waste departments of the Ewo Cotton Mill in Yangshupu have gradually ceased operations due to slow business, causing opposition from more than 500 workers in both departments. They petitioned the party and government organs. Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, the party and government organs specifically convened both labor and management at the Social Bureau for mediation. Twelve labor representatives, including Li Jia'an, Zhao Qifen, Liu Jian, and Yao Changzhao, and management representatives, including foreman Wang Guoxiang, Dai Youheng, an officer from the Civil Training Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters, attended. The mediation was presided over by Zhu Jintao, a mediator from the Social Bureau. The results of the mediation were: (1) The velvet department of Ewo Cotton Mill is permitted to cease operations due to slow business. (2) The 416 workers in the silk waste department, including Ji Jia'an, will be provided with four yuan each for travel expenses to return to their hometowns, with Wang Jiekui, Wang Guoxiang, Wang Shibao, and other foremen of the department responsible. Both parties approved the results, and the dispute was resolved.

(5) For share subscriptions, in addition to shareholders having priority, participation from all sectors is welcome. Tea and refreshments were served after the meeting, and the atmosphere was joyous.

The Eighth District Party Headquarters Requests Exemption from Sampan Monthly Dues 139

There are more than one hundred sampans in Wusong, specializing in ferrying passengers. The boatmen are mostly poor and their income is barely enough to make a living. After the January 28th Incident, they suffered severe losses, and their post-war lives are desolate, making it difficult for them to make ends meet. They are unable to afford the license fees and monthly dues levied by the municipal government. They once petitioned the Eighth District Party Headquarters to negotiate with the municipal government for a reduction. The municipal government stated that the license fees were solely for the actual cost of issuing licenses, and the monthly dues were already at the lowest rate and could not be reduced further. The boatmen, who survived the calamity, find it difficult to survive while burdened with these dues. Recently, the Eighth District Party Headquarters has petitioned the Municipal Party Headquarters to negotiate with the municipal government for the exemption of Wusong sampan monthly dues for this year to provide some relief. If approved, it would greatly benefit the sampan owners.

Resolution of the Rent Increase Dispute in Fengyu Lane 140

The Fengyu Lane houses on Pousse Road in the French Concession are owned by the Chinese Dali Company and managed by lawyer Qiu Fenling as the rental agent. As the houses have been built for eight years, the original rent was not high. This time, an abrupt notice was issued, increasing the rent by 20-30%, which was opposed by the tenants. The negotiations between the two parties lasted for more than a month. It is now reported that the tenants publicly elected Tong Lizhang as their representative to request concessions from the landlord. The landlord has agreed to make a reduction and moderately increase the rent, with a standard increase of two yuan per room, implemented simultaneously within the lane. The tenants in the market houses have no objection, so the matter has been peacefully resolved.

Recent Events at the First Special Court 141

Expansion of the Announcement Area

Addition of a Courtroom

Guo Yun'guan, President of the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, previously jointly established a bi-institutional daily with the Second Branch of the High Court to facilitate litigation for the people. After its discontinuation, notices and announcements were posted in the announcement area for the public to read. Now, because the original wall area was insufficient, the announcement area has been greatly expanded to include the entire wall outside the court, and it has been categorized to make it easy for people to understand at a glance. In addition, President Guo felt that the existing thirteen courtrooms were still insufficient, so he converted a room opposite New Star, formerly used as a lawyer's lounge, into a courtroom. It has now been fully renovated and furnished, and named the Fourteenth Courtroom, specializing in hearing civil cases. Although the room is small, the air is sufficient. As for the damaged walls, windows, and doors in the court, they have all been repaired by hired workers, and all places have been painted and brushed, making them look brand new. Recently, due to the Western New Year, the police have suspended the delivery of criminal public prosecution cases, so the court has felt a little quieter, and the number of vehicles entering and leaving has suddenly decreased. Guo took advantage of this opportunity to repair the dilapidated pavement in the courtyard, hiring many workers to repair it day and night, aiming to complete the work before Monday next week.

Trial of a Large Group of Robbers 142

Shen Yuzhou, a Chinese detective of the Yangshupu Police Department, and detective Shan Zhaoxian, previously arrested robbers Chen Youming, Wu Xingchang, Li Xiaowu, Xia Changfa, Chen Shengcai, Xing Fusheng, Xing Baoxiang, Wu Jinfa, Shen Wenqing, Zhang Xiaofu, Yang Qing'san, Zhou Shenhai, and the woman Sun Shao'shi, etc., seized two pistols and twelve bullets, and handed them over to the First Special District Local Court for trial and detention. After investigation by the Chinese and Western detectives in charge of this case, it was found that the defendants had been involved in armed robberies between December of last year and February 9th of this year, robbing Liu Genying at No. 147 Zhoujia Road, Huang Zongbang at No. 191 Linqing Road, the monk Pan in a bungalow on Meizhou Road, Chen Liu'shi at No. 781 Xinzha Road, Zhou A'fu at No. 175 Qiwupu Road, and other households of gold jewelry and clothing worth over 700 yuan. Part of the original stolen goods was recovered. Yesterday, the police escorted the defendants to the First Special Court for continued trial by Judge Wu Zehan. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin explained the case, stating that defendant Yang Qing'san is currently in the hospital suffering from severe typhoid fever, which is life-threatening. According to the doctor, unless there is a major change, treatment will take three weeks before he can appear in court. Therefore, a postponement is requested. Defendant Sun Shao'shi hired a lawyer to appear in court and requested bail pending trial. The police lawyer opposed, saying that defendant Sun Shao'shi is actually a key criminal who helped the robbers carry pistols privately during the robberies, so bail cannot be agreed to. After Judge Wu questioned the defendants briefly, he ordered them to be returned to custody separately for a retrial at a later date.

Fire in Yangjing Town, Pudong 143

—A Total of Seven Houses Were Burned Down—

Shen Hengxing Oil Mill, No. 1 Youche Street, South End of the Central Market, Yangjing Town, Pudong, is owned by Shen Shunying, a local resident. Shen is old, so the business is managed by his eldest son, Jin Jin. Shen's second son, Quan Duo, died six years ago, leaving behind a wife, Sheng, 40 years old, and a son, Xingyuan, 20 years old. Xingyuan married a Jia girl two years ago. However, because the rooms in the oil mill were insufficient for accommodation, three new bungalows were built across the street last year, specifically for Xingyuan and his wife to live in. Recently, Xingyuan went to Hangzhou to purchase goods, and his wife also returned to Ningbo, so the house was uninhabited. Unexpectedly, at around 3:00 AM yesterday morning, when the old clerk in the oil mill got up to work, he suddenly saw thick smoke and flames shooting out of the empty house. He quickly realized that the interior was ablaze and impossible to extinguish. He urgently reported to the police and called for help. The fire quickly spread to the roof and then to the adjacent Xisongji Winery, and the fire became even more intense, making it difficult to control for a while. Soon, the Yangjing Fire Brigade drove to the scene to extinguish the fire. After a while, the Pudong District Fire Brigade of Lan'ni Du Dongchang Road received the alarm and also drove a pumper truck to help put out the fire. The fire burned until dawn, burning down the three empty bungalows where Xingyuan lived, three houses in the winery, and a large oil mill basket shed and warehouse one after another. The fire gradually went out. The fire trucks stopped extinguishing the fire at around 7:00 AM. After the fire was extinguished, the police and members of the Security Corps who were maintaining order at the scene studied the cause of the fire. They all could not understand how the fire started since the house was empty and uninhabited.

Gong Ziliang Loses His Life Due to the Difficulty of Being a Husband Between Two Women 144

Gong Ziliang, a 35-year-old resident of Songjiang, worked as a driver for the China General Omnibus Company. He married a Wang woman many years ago. Recently, Gong met a young woman, Qian, outside, and they became deeply attached to each other. He then imitated the family of Qi people and set up a small family at No. 860 Yingxun Road, Lukia浜, Nanshi. Unexpectedly, there was no harmony of Qi people. After his wife, Wang, found out, she often stirred up a storm of jealousy, and the family had no peace. The day before yesterday, a major disturbance occurred between the two women. Seeing this situation, Gong deeply regretted his self-inflicted disaster and self-seeking trouble. In a moment of anger, he ingested raw opium and lay in bed waiting to die. He groaned incessantly when the poison took effect, and he died before he could be rescued. He died at Qian's place, so when Wang learned of her husband's death, she rushed to the scene crying and making a scene, so the police took both of them to the police station for questioning. During the interrogation, both women were crestfallen and secretly shedding tears, but it was too late. The director then summoned the head of the 27th Ward, Tao Rong, to report to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Zheng and others arrived at the scene to conduct the autopsy and ordered the body to be collected.

Zhang A'cai Suddenly Assassinated 147

—Shot and Killed While Leaning Against a Fence—

Zhang A'yan, a resident of Shaoxing, lived at No. 7 Taipingfang, Hongzhen. He had a son named Zhang A'cai, 19 years old, who worked at the Yicheng Peng Grain Store on Broadway Road. A week ago, he had a quarrel with the young owner of the Rongqing Bicycle Shop. Later, they each invited gangsters to mediate and settle the matter. The young owner, being in the wrong, offered wine as an apology. At around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, the young owner came and invited A'cai out, but he did not return until late. At around 12:00 AM, someone was suddenly shot and killed on the bamboo fence of the Youlian Film Company on East Tiyu Road, Zhabei. Shen Fengqi of the company heard the gunshot and went out to see. He vaguely saw four people running away. The murdered person was leaning against the bamboo fence and had already died. At that time, it was unknown who it was. He immediately reported to the police chief of the Baziqiao Police Station in the Fifth District. The police arrived and found a business card of Yicheng Peng Grain Store near the deceased. They immediately sent the police to summon the Zhang family from the store, who identified the deceased as Zhang A'cai. They then informed his father, who arrived at the scene and cried bitterly, and recounted a series of events. In addition to reporting to the headquarters, the police station ordered Wang Jinfu, the local guarantor of the 91st district, to report to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Zheng Qinming, coroner Xuan Zhiming, and others arrived at the scene. The autopsy revealed that the deceased was wearing a blue cloth short shirt and trousers, with a white twill short shirt and trousers underneath. The bullet entered the lung through the left breast and did not exit. He was definitely captured and shot at point-blank range. The family members were ordered to collect the body and await the investigation of the murderers and their arrest and prosecution.

The Case of the Murder of the Young Owner of Qian Feng Tai Incense Shop 149

The Incident Seemed to Be a Shooting During a Wallet Robbery

The Manager Chen Qiancheng's Injuries Are Critical

At 9:45 PM the night before last, Chen Zhikui, the young owner of Qian Feng Tai Incense Shop, No. 52 Rue du Pont, French Concession, a native of Ningbo, was shot and killed by thugs when he returned to the shop from outside and walked into the small alley next door. Chen Qiancheng, the manager of the shop, was also shot three times and went to Renji Hospital for treatment. The police sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Yanshi Office to await an autopsy. The details of the incident have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. The details of the incident are as follows: That night, the deceased, Chen Zhikui, sent goods to Hongkou and returned to the shop by rickshaw for a short rest. He then left the shop and wanted to go to his home upstairs, detouring to the small alley next to the north. As he stepped into the alley, a man in a jacket followed Chen behind. Chen turned around and asked where he was going. The man replied that he was going upstairs to look for Wang Liutang. The remaining rooms on the upper floor of the shop had been rented to Wang Liutang and his wife in September of last year for 16 yuan per month. Wang was a gangster. Chen did not pay attention because he heard that he was looking for Wang. He took about two or three steps forward and met his 11-year-old sister, Lin Di. Chen asked his sister where she was going. His sister replied that her mother had sent her to buy cigarettes. Chen also asked his sister to buy a pack of cigarettes and took out a cigarette and handed it to the person behind him. He then touched his wallet behind him (containing about 70-80 yuan in cash) to get money for his sister. Unexpectedly, the wallet was suddenly lost. Chen suspected that the person behind him had stolen it. He turned around and asked him to return the wallet, saying that he could treat him if he returned the wallet. The man replied that he had not stolen his wallet. But Chen suspected that he wanted to search his body. At this time, the man took out a pistol from his sleeve and fired at Chen. The bullet hit his throat. The murderer turned around and fled out of the alley. Chen, who was shot, spurted blood and chased out of the alley, shouting for help. After leaving the alley, he ran south to the corner of the vegetable market street and collapsed in front of the Nanhuo store and died. At this time, Chen Qiancheng, the manager of the store, heard the shouts of the young owner and saw the blood flowing from his throat, and saw the murderer running north. He chased after him, but was shot three times by the murderer, hitting his right shoulder, right leg, and lower abdomen. He fell to the ground. The murderer then fled into Baoyu Lane. The colleagues in the Qian Feng Tai store hired a car to send Qiancheng to the hospital for treatment first. The police were alerted and immediately sent detectives to round up the murderer, but he had disappeared. The body was then transported to the Yanshi Office. Yesterday morning, the police reported to the Second Special Court to assign Prosecutor Deng, forensic doctor Jiang Xuan, and secretary Zhao Yifen to the office to examine the body, ascend to the court, and according to the testimony of witness Hong Xiangxian (a clerk in Qian Feng Tai), and Chen Chen, the mother of the deceased, requested to arrest the murderer and seek redress. Deng decreed that Chen Zhikui had been shot and killed, and the body was collected by the family members. The police station will arrest the murderer and bring him to justice. It is reported that Chen Qiancheng is now in critical condition in the hospital. Chen Tingchun, the father of the deceased, is still in Hankou. The store has sent a telegram urging him to come to Shanghai to take care of the funeral affairs.

Li Chengyi, the standing director of the bank, and Huang Boqiao, the director of the Jinghu-Huhangyong Railway Bureau, also visited the site.

Dr. Muehlens of Germany to Give Lectures 150

Dr. Muehlens of Germany is an expert in the study of tropical diseases. He is a scholar with deep knowledge and one of the leading scholars in Europe. He is currently a professor at the University of Hamburg in Germany and the director of the Tropical Disease Research Institute. The League of Nations has hired him to come to China to investigate health matters. He arrived in Shanghai on the 10th of this month. Liu Ruiheng, Director of the Nanjing Health Department, specially entrusted Weng Zhilong, President of Tongji University, and Li Ting'an, Director of the Shanghai Health Bureau, to entertain him. Many listeners were present. There were also scientific films to add to the fun. It is reported that the doctor plans to continue lecturing in Shanghai for several days. He has scheduled to lecture on spirochetology and battlefield hygiene in English again at Shanghai Medical College on the 14th and 17th. Afterwards, he will continue to lecture at the Medical College of Tongji University (i.e., Baolong Hospital). He is scheduled to lecture on oncology at 6:30 PM on the 18th, on dysentery at 6:00 PM on the 19th, and on malaria at 4:00 PM on the 20th. Lin Ronghan Invents Magnetic Sheet Photography 151

Photos are Printed on Magnetic Sheets

Never Fade or Change Color

According to Shenshi Telegraph News Agency's local news, Mr. Lin Ronghan, a Cantonese who served as the Director of the Automobile Transportation Department of the 19th Route Army during the January 28th Incident, is well-versed in photographic art. In view of the lack of photographic burning techniques on Chinese porcelain sheets and image printing on Fuzhou lacquerware, and the fact that porcelain photos on the market are all hand-painted and then burned, so it is uncertain whether they resemble the original. It is even more difficult to make artistic photos with complex backgrounds. In view of this, Mr. Lin has been working hard for four or five years and has finally succeeded. From now on, photos can be directly printed on porcelain sheets, which are exactly the same as the original photos. After the film is printed, it is burned at a very high temperature, so that the photo penetrates into the porcelain plate. Even if it is washed with water or scraped with a knife, it will not fade or change color. Once the photo is printed on this porcelain sheet, it can be permanently preserved, avoiding the risk of contamination and discoloration. This invention will add a lot of color to the artistic community in our country. It is reported that Mr. Lin has decided to make this invention public and will display his products at Wangkai Photo Studio on Nanjing Road soon for the public to view, and entrust it to its manager.

Responsibility Statement on Meat Inspection Detention Cases in the Freight Industry 153

Water Patrol Team Notifies to Detain at Any Time

Expresses Helplessness to the Guild

The Shanghai Health Bureau's implementation of inspection and detention of cured ham and goods has been strongly opposed by the two industries. Recently, it has also aroused the dissatisfaction of various industry associations, providing strong assistance to the two industries of cured ham. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Although this case has been presented to the Executive Yuan by the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce on behalf of both industries for instructions, there has been no reply to date. Now, the freight industry and Datong Company, etc., have stated that because the ham and cured meat they transport have been detained for a long time, they are afraid that the goods will be damaged, and they have a heavy responsibility. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the ham industry association stating everything, which is recorded as follows:

Statement of the Freight Association 154

To: The case of the Tongli Company and other freight companies states that, for the case of the Shanghai Health Bureau's import inspection of meat, the ham industry is striving to abolish it. Recently, our company and others have transported more than one hundred pieces of ham and wind meat from Hangzhou to Shanghai. Because each ham shop refuses to accept it before the definite resolution, it is now stored in the road bureau freight yard and in the open air. It is still difficult to predict when it will be delivered. Each ham shop has been notified that the storage fees will be recognized in accordance with the regulations, but if this solution is indefinitely, it will be stacked for a long time. If it happens to be rotted, rat-injured, etc., our company will be difficult to bear this heavy responsibility. It is specially requested to forward the letter to the Shanghai Ham Industry Association and inform each shop to check. In the future, if the above-mentioned accidents occur in the stacked goods, each ham shop shall be responsible for itself. Our company and others will not be responsible for anything else except for handling the stacking. Please forward it, and it will be impossible to thank you, etc. The goods carried by our industry have always been delivered immediately after the goods arrive, which is a fixed procedure. This time, each ham shop has not been able to pick up the arrived goods due to the unresolved meat import inspection, which is a special situation. However, if it is delayed for a long time, it will cause damage. The responsibility issue in this regard should also be declared in advance to avoid disputes. The reason for the letter is as stated above. Correspondingly, the letter is hereby forwarded. All goods have been delayed for a long time, resulting in damage, and our industry cannot be responsible. Please check with your association, forward it to each shop, and wait for a reply.

Datong Company's Report 155

To: At 4:00 PM today, the water patrol team came with a letter from the Health Bureau, stating that all imported salted meat and ham from each shop are not allowed to be picked up without inspection, and our company is responsible for detaining them at any time. Otherwise, our company will be asked to pick up the goods, etc. Our company has been in contact with your association for many years, and the relationship is very close. Since the inspection occurred, inspectors have come here to discuss it. Our company believes that it is difficult to detain goods due to business concerns. Please forgive us. Now we are notified by the water police that detention for inspection is imperative. Since this responsibility is assigned to our company, we are helpless. We specially inform your association and quickly forward it to your colleagues to check, so as to avoid misunderstandings. April 13th,

The Ham Industry Association and the Cured Meat Industry Association have also blocked the river of pig carcasses, totaling more than 6,000, with an estimated value of more than 100,000 gold. If it is delayed for a long time, the sacrifices will be immeasurable. For this reason, both industries have scheduled an emergency joint meeting to discuss countermeasures.

Petition to the Municipal Government by Ship-Dwelling Refugees on the Zhabei Suzhou Creek 158

Yesterday morning, more than 30 representatives, including Gao Longyou, were sent by the ship-dwelling refugees on the Suzhou Creek to the Municipal Government with a petition. Mr. Xu, a clerk from the Second Section of the Municipal Government, received them. The representatives detailed their suffering under the strict ban and requested the Water Patrol to postpone enforcement, etc. Mr. Xu replied that he would submit the petition to the mayor for review and then relay the instructions back to the ships. The original text of the petition is recorded below:

We, the refugees, humbly submit this petition. Due to years of unusual drought in our hometowns, we had no means of survival and were forced to sell our land and buy boats, bringing our elderly and young children to Shanghai to live on small boats along the banks of the Suzhou Creek. We use the boats as homes, temporary precarious nests. The men pull rickshaws, the women reel silk, and some even do the most arduous labor. Now, the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau has requested the government to issue an order to immediately ban our ship-dwelling, leaving us with no food to return and in violation of orders if we stay. We have no money to move ashore or rent houses, and selling our boats would leave us temporarily homeless, virtually trapping us in a desperate situation. We believe that even in times of war and chaos, those without homes on land or water could still find refuge. Now, in this unified world, we cannot even allow these destitute people to live in temporary peace. Those with benevolence should not bear to see this. We have long admired your government's compassionate heart and its commitment to the welfare of the common people. Therefore, we have sent representatives to your government to seek your consideration and beg for relief measures and a postponement of the ban, so that we can find a way to relocate without being forced into desperation. We will be eternally grateful.

Special Article: Biography of Mr. Ye Chengzhong 163

Ye Chengzhong, also known as Chengzhong, was from Zhenhai, Zhejiang. His mother's surname was Hong, and his father was called Zhiyu, who was a farmer.

When he was six years old, his father died. He had two brothers, and they depended on their mother, but the family was extremely poor, with only a dilapidated house left. The mother and sons were constantly threatened by hunger and cold. When he was nine years old, he was able to attend school, but he dropped out after only half a year due to poverty. This fact gave his young mind a strong stimulation. From then on, he understood the difficulty for poor children to acquire knowledge, and at the same time, he experienced the pain of poor children dropping out of school. This understanding and experience were the distant cause of his later founding of the Chengzhong Mongolian School.

At the age of eleven, he entered a neighboring oil mill as a worker. After three years, he quit because the treatment was too harsh. After leaving the oil mill, life was even harder, even without means of survival. Mr. Ni, a fellow villager, pitied his plight and respected his sincerity, so he invited him to Shanghai. At that time, the travel expenses from Zhenhai to Shanghai were only 2,000 yuan, but even these 2,000 yuan were obtained by his mother mortgaging the autumn rice in the field. This difficult situation and hardship was the driving force for his later efforts to achieve success.

After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Ni recommended him to work as an apprentice in a grocery store in the French Concession. At this time, it was after the Opium War, and the imperialists had used warships to open the door of our country. Shanghai had also been opened as a commercial port. Foreign merchant ships gathered in the Huangpu River. Every morning, he would drive a small boat, loaded with groceries, and sell them to foreign merchant ships, and after returning to the store, he had to sweep and cook. He had no rest for a moment all day. He spent three years in this state of life, and then quit because of the shopkeeper's stupidity. At this time, he was already seventeen years old. Three years of apprenticeship had given him a slight understanding of how to make a living, and further determined his determination to live independently. So this time he left the grocery store was the starting point of his independent life, and also the beginning of his career.

After leaving the grocery store, he still drove a small boat, shouting and selling in the Huangpu River. He was as hardworking and enduring as he was in the store before. After a long time, he learned the skills of doing business. More importantly, he understood that the ships gathered in the Huangpu River were all weapons for invading China. This understanding was a turning point in his thinking, and made him make a great wish to repair the loopholes and regain the rights and interests.

In 1826, that is, the first year of Tongzhi in the former Qing Dynasty, he tried his best to raise funds and began to set up a small store in Hongkou. In the winter of that year, he moved to Outer Hongkou. The small-scale operation naturally yielded very meager profits. However, he was able to be hardworking and enduring internally, and to treat people with sincerity externally, building up credit in the market. In this way, his business became more and more prosperous, and the scale also expanded. The small store in Outer Hongkou, which was limited in scale, had branches all over the country in a few years. Mr. Ye, who was formerly poor and unable to support himself, had now become a powerful leader in the national business community. This success was naturally due to his diligence, thrift, self-discipline, honest treatment of others, and extraordinary talent and energy. "Where there is a will, there is a way." Who says Mr. Ye's success was accidental?

However, Mr. Ye's true success is more than that, and his true career is not limited to that, because he realized that in order to repair the loopholes and regain the rights and interests, commercial competition was still the second step, and the most important thing was to revitalize domestic industry. Only by revitalizing industry can we resist the invasion of foreign products, and only by revitalizing industry can we engage in commercial competition. Therefore, he founded match factories and silk reeling factories in Shanghai and Hankou on a large scale. This was our country's early match industry and silk reeling industry. In fact, at that time, although the capitalist advanced countries in Europe had developed into imperialism and were intensifying the opening and competition for overseas markets, China, which was stagnating in the agricultural economy, was their target of competition. However, at that time, the power of the capitalist powers in China was still very weak, and the foundation was not yet stable. If we could take advantage of this time to rise up and reform, it would not be too late. The Meiji Restoration movement in Japan in 1868 was a good example. However, the Qing government at that time was never able to realize it, and although there was the "Hundred Days' Reform" in 1898, it ultimately failed due to the oppression of the old forces. From then on, the imperialists' attack on our country became more and more fierce, and their power in China also grew stronger. Under this situation, our country's agricultural economy was increasingly collapsing, and the national industry was unable to lift its head due to the imperialists' constraints. In the process of continuous decay and collapse and continuous infringement, China finally fell into a semi-colonial status, which it has not been able to extricate itself from to this day. This may be something that Mr. Ye did not expect at first. However, it is precisely for this reason that Mr. Ye's vision is even more remarkable.

Secondly, what deserves our attention most in Mr. Ye's career is that he "accumulates wealth and is able to distribute wealth." He is not used by money, not burdened by money, and can make the society's money still be used for the society. In his later years, he built the Huaide Hall to shelter orphans and widows, the Zhongxiao Hall to shelter relatives, and set up charity schools and smallpox bureaus to shelter the very poor. Other projects such as promoting academies, dredging water conservancy, managing roads, repairing bridges, building the Chongyi Association and the Guangyi Association, and providing disaster relief to the provinces of Feng, Jin, Yu, Yan, Lu, Su, and Zhe, he made generous donations to all. Among them, what we should particularly mention is the establishment of this school.

This school, Chengzhong Middle School, was originally called Chengzhong Mongolian School. Due to the stimulation of dropping out of school at a young age, Mr. Ye donated 28 acres of land in Zhangjiawan, Hongkou, and 100,000 taels of silver to found Chengzhong Mongolian School, so that poor children could have the opportunity to study. When the construction plan was about to begin, Mr. Ye suddenly fell ill and died. Before he died, he repeatedly told his family members, "After I die, you must complete my ambition to found the Mongolian School." He also left a letter to the school directors Fan Fen and Chen Zuli, saying, "Chengzhong was poor and orphaned, and regrets that he dropped out of school. He has long wanted to establish a school to help poor children. The matter is just beginning, but the end is approaching. Gentlemen, we have known each other for a long time and must be able to understand my humble wishes and work together to accomplish this." This was in 1899, that is, the 25th year of Guangxu in the former Qing Dynasty.

The following year, in 1900, Mr. Ye's son, Yijian, inherited his father's will and donated another 100,000 taels of silver. In 1902, Mr. Yizhao, Yiming, Yiquan, Yiqi, Yiyong, and Yiyu also jointly donated 100,000 taels of silver. The school building started construction in 1900 (September of the 26th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty) and was completed in 1901 (January of the 27th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty). The school opened on April 16 of the same year (February 28 of the 27th year of Guangxu). This is the origin of this school, and it is also Mr. Ye's greatest and immortal career. We, the faculty and students of this school, look up to the portrait of Mr. Ye Chengzhong today and recall that nine-year-old child who dropped out of school due to poverty, the eleven-year-old child who worked in the oil mill, and the young man who drove a small boat and shouted and sold in the Huangpu River. His lifelong hard work has given us the opportunity to study today. How should we work hard and how should we be diligent in order to live up to Mr. Ye Chengzhong's original wishes? Look, isn't Mr. Ye Chengzhong's portrait urging us every day, morning and evening, and expecting us?

Mr. Ye Chengzhong's life is synonymous with struggle. His success is due to his willingness to struggle. He has a torch-like vision and boiling enthusiasm. His career and his personality can never be praised by the "feather decorations," "second-rank official hats," "Grand Master Ronglu," or other irrelevant honorary titles after his death. The founding of this school alone is enough for him to be immortal.

Mr. Ye Chengzhong was born on July 18, 1840 (June 20 of the Gengzi year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty) and died on November 5, 1899 (October 3 of the Yihai year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty). Chen Binhe, 32nd anniversary of the founding of Chengzhong Middle School.

Letters to the Editor 164

To the Editor, On the 14th, my lawyer acted as an agent for Huang Zhou in the case of Huang Zhou suing Xi Longsheng for confirmation of mother and son. During the debate, the two lawyers, Li, listed as witnesses in Huang Zhou's statement, are now also acting as agents for the defendant Xi Longsheng. Therefore, they are exercising the duties of lawyers in the position of witnesses, which conflicts with the obligations and responsibilities that witnesses should fulfill. There is a risk of bias. Article 32 of the Civil Procedure Law stipulates that judges should recuse themselves from performing duties in litigation cases in which they have been litigation agents, witnesses, or appraisers. The state's restrictions on the exercise of duties by court staff are so strict, let alone lawyers who are specialized professionals. Therefore, my lawyer advocates stopping the agency rights of the two lawyers, Li and Qin, in this case. If a witness acts as a lawyer, then the lawyer is an employee. As long as there is a public fee, the lawyer will do everything possible to defend the interests of the client, and it is inevitable that he will be biased. This was the original intention of my lawyer's debate at the time. However, your newspaper only stated, "Lawyer Zhang also said that a lawyer is an employee. As long as he is given money, he will do anything." This is a distorted and untrue statement, and should be corrected to avoid misunderstanding. I hereby request that this letter be published in the "Letters to the Editor" column for correction. Sincerely, Lawyer Zhang Shewo, April 15.

To the Editor, I have just read the news in your newspaper that "the city will switch to automatic telephones," which states that it will "benefit all users in the city, the cost will not increase, and a temporary contract will be signed on the 18th." This was not mentioned at the time, and I am afraid it will cause misunderstanding. I am hereby sending a letter to request a correction. To the Editor, Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, April 15.
