Readers' Advisor

Regarding the Discussion Letters on the Question of "Can One Return to the Countryside?" 168

(9) Letter from Wei Mingjun of Nanjing: Speaking of the Youth's Way Out from the Rural Problem

Mr. Reporter, I have some simple opinions regarding the question of "returning to the countryside." I request your guidance. To answer the question "Can one return to the countryside?", we should first clearly ask "Why do we want to return to the countryside?" By recognizing the essence of the problem, we can avoid answering the wrong question and provide a relatively correct answer. According to Mr. Xiongsheng's original intention, because in the city he is "suffering from the most fashionable disease: unemployment, and feeling the pain of having no confidence in finding a job," he raised a question: "Can one return to the countryside and find the most appropriate and possible way to make a living?" From this, we know that Mr. Xiongsheng, who wants to return to the countryside, has the same reason as the peasants who left the countryside: they are forced and driven by the ruthless reality of life. It is not because of "love" or "dislike" of the countryside. The peasants left the clean, honest, and free (?) land, not because they "cannot resolutely endure hardship in the countryside to seek a living." On the contrary, even if they resolutely endure hardship in the countryside to seek a living, they still cannot find a place to live. From the increasing overpopulation in the city, we can see the gradual increase in the rate of peasants leaving the village. The continuous increase in the import of major grains further shows the declining rural economy in China. The essence of the countryside has been exploited for thousands of years and flowed into the city (especially Shanghai) with the gentry, officials, and into the banks (especially foreign banks). In this way, the Chinese countryside has become an empty cellar, which has long been looted clean. We want the unemployed in the city to run to this cellar to find a way out. What can they find? Mr. Reporter is right: "Running to the countryside to solve life problems will only result in remaining hungry and becoming a rural unemployed person." In terms of making a living, returning to the countryside is just a dead end. Mr. Xiongsheng will undoubtedly only be disappointed. Speaking of Mr. You Huai’gao's theory of saving the country through rural education, this is another topic. Although he wants to solve Mr. Xiongsheng's problem through this, he has not hit the point. Because the first step of his plan is for Mr. Xiongsheng to borrow at least 100 yuan from a friend at the tax office as capital. However, Mr. Xiongsheng clearly stated that he is a "complete proletarian." I think if he could "borrow at least 100 yuan" at once, he could at least rely on these relatives and friends to think of a way to stay in the city, instead of "sighing at the ocean and having no way" and thinking of returning to the countryside. Seeing the beggars on the roadside, he scolded them for being too lazy and unmotivated, and why they didn't find some money to do small business and earn a living by their own efforts. This is such a straightforward statement. Let's take a step back. Mr. You can "design" to borrow this batch of capital for Mr. Xiongsheng. Can this batch of capital make a huge profit and maintain one person's life for three or four years? Can it support "the old mother above and the wife and children below?" That's right, Mr. You has a lot of designs. He wants to charge a tuition fee of one yuan per section. He wants each child to pay one chicken, one duck, or thirty eggs to the school every year. Can every peasant family in the impoverished countryside afford this? Has Mr. You ever known how many peasants in each village do not have "one yuan" hidden on them all year round? How many peasant families don't even have food to feed chickens or ducks, and are forced to sell chickens, ducks, and their eggs at low prices in exchange for a temporary full meal? How many families can take the surplus wealth to let you city unemployed "wear Zhongshan suits" and "wear cloth robes," and support you, "a leader standing out from the crowd," to "save the country through rural education?" The illusion is finally shattered by reality. As for Mr. You wanting to use bank loans as a "very solid" foundation, this is even more of an illusion. The bank's capital flows for profit. If it can be the foundation of your career, why doesn't he, the banker, go to "absolutely advocate and implement efforts to save the country through rural education?" According to our recent experience, we only know that bank loans require a large number of agricultural products as collateral, village gentry and wealthy people as guarantees, and more than one percent interest per year. And if it is not repaid on time, the collateral will be sold, and the surplus will be confiscated. Not enough to compensate. Moreover, what guarantee does a city unemployed youth have to borrow money from the bank? Even if you borrow money by various means, you are only helping the bank to do the work of re-exploiting the peasants, and doing the work of accelerating the collapse of the rural economy. You will not wait until "students grow up in three or four years," but see your employer and your students, "future believers," displaced and wandering in the ravines, away from your "illusion" by 18,000 feet. Mr. You is not only very knowledgeable about rural education, but also a master of utopianism who uses "imagination" to avoid reality. Mr. Xiongsheng, Mr. Reporter, and dear readers, please give a fair criticism. In short, based on Mr. Xiongsheng's motivation, one cannot return to the countryside. According to Mr. You's "imagination," returning to the countryside is also a dead end. Of course, the countryside has its own historical destiny, and it will not leave the various stages that it must go through in its evolution because someone comes to prosper it or not. At the same time, Mr. Xiongsheng's suffering is the common suffering of his contemporaries. If he does not have a bit of courage to survive and is always so cowardly as to "have no courage to commit crimes and no courage to commit suicide," the only way out may be to starve to death. We are very surprised. Why can't a youth in this era face the common enemy of society and fight, but instead succumb to a corner, fantasizing about the arrival of a savior, or waiting for death?

Carrying a Large Number of Comfort Items and a Thousand Broadswords

The Shandong education circle, because the soldiers at the front line are fighting against Japan and shedding blood on the battlefield, specially initiated a fundraising campaign to comfort the troops to fulfill the national duty. All educational personnel in the province, hearing the news, enthusiastically contributed. In the shortest period of time, 14,500 yuan has been raised. It was decided to use 5,000 yuan in cash to comfort the wounded soldiers, use 5,000 yuan to purchase items to donate to the soldiers at the front line, and make another 1,000 broadswords to send to the front for killing the enemy. At 3 pm on the 12th, the three representatives of the education circle, Sun Dongsheng, Xu Bopu, and Wang Lifu, had already carried the cash and 1,000 sets of trousers and jackets, 2,000 straw sandals, 10,000 towels, 2,400 pairs of socks, 5,000 burlap bags, and more than 2,000 catties of pickles, and took the 10th train on the Jinpu Railway north. Students from the Second Provincial Experimental Primary School donated a pair of socks and a towel, specifically to be given to Song Zheyuan, the commander of the 29th Army. Next, the Kuangshi Sanyi Yong Burlap Bag Company donated 1,000 burlap bags, which were also handed over to the representatives to take with them. He Siyuan, Director of the Education Department, and Wang Jinxin, Secretary-General, and others went to the station to see them off when the representatives went north and took care of everything. Mr. He also sent a telegram to He Yingqin and Chiang Kai-shek of the Beiping Military Affairs Committee, asking them to take care of them.

Regulations for Primary and Secondary Schools and Normal Schools (11) 172

Article 111: Those who have one of the following circumstances shall not be employed as teachers in normal schools: (1) Those who have violated criminal law and the evidence is conclusive; (2) Those who have poor academic performance; (3) Those who have deserted their duties; (4) Those who are negligent in training and school affairs; (5) Those who suffer from mental illness or have chronic diseases that prevent them from working; (6) Those who have improper behavior or bad habits.

Article 112: After a normal school teacher has worked in the school for nine consecutive years, they may take a one-year sabbatical to engage in research and investigation and must submit the results to the school to be submitted to the provincial and municipal education administrative organs or submitted to the county and city education administrative organs to be forwarded to the provincial education department for verification. During the sabbatical of the aforementioned teachers, they should still receive their original salary, but only if they do not concurrently hold any paid positions. Article 112: The education administrative organs of each province and city shall formulate measures to facilitate the further education of normal school teachers and report them to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation.

Article 114: The examination, employment, and protection of normal school teachers shall be determined by separate regulations.

Article 115: The salary scale and seniority salary increase methods for normal school teachers shall be determined by the competent education administrative organs and submitted directly or forwarded to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation. The lowest level of the aforementioned teacher salary scale should refer to local conditions to ensure that it can maintain an appropriate standard of living.

Article 116: The principal of a normal school shall be paid three to five levels higher than the full-time teachers, as determined by the competent education administrative organ.

Article 117: The pension and compensation methods for normal school staff shall be handled in accordance with the National Government's promulgated regulations on pensions and compensation for school staff.

Chapter 14: Attached Primary Schools and Kindergartens 173

Article 118: Normal schools should establish attached primary schools to facilitate students' practice and experimentation in elementary education and may also establish attached kindergartens.

Article 119: The attached primary school shall have a principal who shall be hired by the principal of the normal school from qualified personnel and reported to the competent education administrative organ for record.

Article 120: The attached primary school and kindergarten should be located near the normal school.

Article 121: The attached primary school should lead the primary schools in nearby counties in the study and experimentation of educational problems in order to improve them.

Article 122: The attached primary school shall be managed in accordance with the Primary School Law and the Primary School Regulations.

Chapter 15: Simple Normal Schools and Simple Normal Departments 174

Article 123: Simple normal schools and simple normal departments shall be established in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of these Regulations. These simple normal schools and simple normal departments shall be discontinued as soon as there are sufficient primary school teachers in the local area.

Article 124: The admission qualification for simple normal schools is graduation from primary school with a study period of four years. The admission qualification for simple normal departments is graduation from junior high school with a study period of one year.

Article 125: Simple normal schools should be established in counties and cities in principle. Article 126: Simple normal schools should be located in rural areas to the extent possible. Simple normal schools located in rural areas may be simplified into rural normal schools. Article 127: The curriculum standards for simple normal schools and simple normal departments shall be determined separately.

Article 128: Simple normal schools and simple normal departments may shorten the vacation period.

Article 129: If there are no attached primary schools or kindergartens for the practice of students in simple normal schools and simple normal departments, they may practice in nearby public and private primary schools and kindergartens.

Article 130: Graduates of simple normal schools and simple normal departments shall serve as teachers in simple primary schools, short-term primary schools, and junior primary schools. After graduates of simple normal schools and simple normal departments have completed their service period and have excellent grades, they may enter normal schools and kindergarten normal departments to study, but they must still pass the entrance examination.

Article 131: A simple normal school shall have a principal who shall preside over school affairs and teach classes. The time spent may be no less than one-half of the minimum full-time teaching time. The weekly teaching hours for full-time teachers in simple normal schools and simple normal departments shall be 22 to 26 hours.

Article 132: A simple normal school shall have one director of instruction, one school doctor, one accountant, and two to four clerks, who shall be hired and employed by the principal separately and reported to the competent education administrative organ for record.

Article 133: The principal of a simple normal school must be of sound character, excellent talent, have research in elementary education, and meet one of the following qualifications: (1) Graduated from a domestic or foreign normal university, university education college, education department, or other departments but have studied 20 credits of education courses and have engaged in educational work for more than two years after graduation and have achieved results; (2) Graduated from a domestic or foreign university bachelor's degree or higher normal bachelor's degree and have engaged in educational work for more than three years and have achieved results; (3) Graduated from a domestic or foreign higher normal vocational school, vocational school, or vocational school bachelor's degree and have engaged in educational work for more than four years and have achieved results.

Article 134: Teachers of simple normal schools must be of sound character, have research in elementary education, and the subject they teach is the subject they specialize in, and meet one of the following qualifications: (1) Those who have passed the normal school teacher examination or assessment; (2) Graduates of domestic or foreign normal universities or university education colleges education departments; (3) Graduates of domestic or foreign university bachelor's degree, higher normal bachelor's degree, vocational school, vocational school, or vocational school bachelor's degree and have more than one year of teaching experience; (4) Those who have graduated from schools equivalent to senior high school and have more than three years of teaching experience and have achieved research results in the subject they teach; (5) Those who have published valuable professional writings; (6) Those who have refined skills (specifically applicable to labor science teachers).

Article 135: Those who have the circumstances in Article 107 and Article 109 of these Regulations shall not be employed as principals and teachers of simple normal schools.

Article 136: Except as specifically stipulated in this chapter, the remaining parts of these Regulations shall apply to simple normal schools and simple normal departments.

Chapter 16 Supplementary Provisions

Article 137: These Regulations may be amended by the Ministry of Education when necessary.

Article 138: These Regulations shall come into effect on August 1, 1933.

Vocational School Regulations Chapter 1 General Provisions 175

Article 1: These Regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Vocational School Law.

Article 2: Vocational schools are places for implementing production education. In accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Vocational School Law, the following training shall be implemented: (1) Strengthening physical fitness; (2) Cultivating civic morality; (3) Developing labor habits; (4) Enriching vocational knowledge and skills; (5) Enhancing vocational ethics; (6) Inspiring entrepreneurial spirit.

Article 3: Vocational schools are divided into junior vocational schools and senior vocational schools. Article 4: Junior vocational schools impart relatively simple production knowledge and skills to young people in order to cultivate their ability to engage in vocational work.

Article 5: Senior vocational schools impart relatively advanced production knowledge and skills to young people in order to cultivate practical production and management talents and lay the foundation for their further research.

Article 6: The admission qualification for junior vocational schools is graduation from primary school or having equivalent education and being between the ages of 12 and 18. The study period is one to three years, which may be shortened as necessary. Article 7: The admission qualification for senior vocational schools is (1) graduation from junior high school or having equivalent education and being between the ages of 15 and 22. The study period is three years; (2) graduation from primary school or having equivalent education and being between the ages of 12 and 20. The study period is five or six years.

Article 8: Vocational schools shall be established separately for one subject in a certain industry in principle (such as ceramics, leather making, dyeing and weaving, or silk weaving, cotton weaving, wool weaving, etc. in industry; animal husbandry, forestry, sericulture, etc. in agriculture). However, with the special approval of the competent education administrative organ, several subjects in the same industry may be established concurrently, or one industry may be established jointly (such as agriculture, industry, commerce, etc.).

Article 9: Vocational schools that are established separately for one subject are called junior or senior vocational schools of a certain subject. Vocational schools that are established concurrently for two subjects are called junior or senior vocational schools of a certain two subjects. Vocational schools that are established jointly for two or more subjects of agriculture, industry, or commerce are called junior or senior agricultural, industrial, or commercial vocational schools. Vocational schools that are established jointly for several industries are called junior or senior vocational schools of a certain industry. Vocational schools that are established jointly for both junior and senior levels are called vocational schools.

Article 10: Vocational schools may, depending on local needs, establish vocational supplementary classes or vocational supplementary schools, the methods of which shall be determined separately.

Article 11: Before junior vocational schools in various places have been fully established, vocational classes may be temporarily attached to primary schools, and subjects may be established depending on local needs, the methods of which shall be determined separately.

Chapter 2 Establishment and Management

Article 12: Junior vocational schools shall be established in counties and cities in principle. The establishment, change, and closure of junior vocational schools shall be first submitted by the county and city competent education administrative organs to the provincial education department for approval based on the actual conditions of the economy, education, industry, and raw materials in and around the school location, and then handled, and reported to the Ministry of Education for record. The aforementioned junior vocational schools may be jointly established by two or more counties due to special local circumstances.

Article 13: Senior vocational schools shall be established in provinces or cities directly under the Executive Yuan in principle. The establishment, change, or closure of senior vocational schools shall be submitted by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs to the Ministry of Education for approval based on the actual conditions of the economy, education, industry, and raw materials in and around the school location, and then handled. The aforementioned senior vocational schools may be established by counties and cities with the approval of the Ministry of Education by the provincial education department due to special local circumstances.

丨　A Discussion Meeting of Student Representatives from Various Schools is Held

丨　Nine Schools Including Shanghai High School Are Selected as Preparatory Committee Members

The Shanghai Middle School Student Union of this city has been virtually suspended since the January 28th Shanghai Incident. Considering the severity of the national crisis, and in order to strengthen the national salvation effort, it is deemed necessary to continue the organization. Details are as follows:

Attending Representatives: Included Wu Shaowei, Song Xianchuan, and Chen Mingzhang from Shanghai High School; Fan Chuanying, Liu Tong, and Wang Zhigang from Datong High School Affiliated; Bai Hai, Tan Xianhuang, and Ren Jikang from Minli High School; Cao Yirong from Chengzhong; Li Chongbi and Wang Degeng from Fudan High School Affiliated; Wu Yingxue, Duanmu Yan, and Wang Shujuan from Shanghai Girls' High School; Tong Wenlong from Huahua; Zhang Jingsong from Huiling, and over twenty others. Wu Shaowei was elected as the temporary chairman, and Wang Zhigang as the recorder.

Key Resolutions: (1) To initiate the organization of the Middle School Student Union; (2) To organize a preparatory committee, and to select Shanghai Provincial Shanghai High School, Fudan High School Affiliated, Minli, Qingxin, Shanghai Baptist University, Shanghai Girls' High School, Huahua, Huiling, and Datong High School Affiliated as the nine schools for the preparatory committee; (3) Shanghai Provincial Shanghai High School will be responsible for convening the first preparatory committee meeting; (4) The preparatory committee's contact address will be temporarily located within Shanghai Provincial Shanghai High School; (5) The first preparatory committee meeting is scheduled for 4 PM on Tuesday, the 18th of this month, at Shanghai High School.

Tianjin-Shanghai Inter-Port Football Match: Shanghai Team Heavily Defeated 1-7 188

Tianjin Wins Due to Home Advantage, Talent, and Teamwork

Jie Hansheng, Defei, and Zhou Xianyan Were the Most Outstanding

Shanghai Will Play the Tianjin Chinese Combined Team Today

(Tianjin, 15th) The Tianjin-Shanghai inter-port football match was held at 3 PM today at the British football field. As a result, Tianjin won by a large margin of 7-1. The spirit of both sides was very good, and the audience was very interested.

Shanghai Lost Two Goals in Ten Minutes 189

In the first five minutes, the Tianjin team launched an offensive, with the left wing being particularly active. With excellent coordination, the Shanghai goal was first breached. In a few minutes, the Tianjin team attacked from the middle again and scored again. Within ten minutes, Shanghai lost two goals in a row.

Twelve-Yard Gate Falls Again: Shanghai Continues to Lose Ground 190

So they played cautiously, and the situation eased slightly. However, Shanghai was soon penalized with a twelve-yard penalty, resulting in a score of 3-0. Tianjin's left inside forward, Jie Hansheng, who was famous at sea a few years ago, scored a goal alone, charging in and scoring with a long shot. It was exceptionally wonderful.

Shanghai Team Finally Scores: Up to this point, Shanghai was heavily defeated 4-0. 191

A few minutes before the end of the first half, Shanghai worked hard to counterattack and got a corner kick, finally scoring and opening Shanghai's account. The score at halftime was Tianjin 4, Shanghai 1.

3-0 in the Second Half 192

Counterattack Fails Again and Loses: After the break, the battle continued. Shanghai was greatly invigorated and counterattacked repeatedly, but to no avail. Tianjin, on the other hand, seized an opportunity and approached the city again. In the melee in front of the goal, Tianjin scored the fifth goal.

Wonderful Pass for Sixth Goal: 193

The outcome of the game seemed to be determined. The battle situation formed a trend of individual actions. Tianjin's offense also slowed down. Just before the end of the game, Tianjin inadvertently passed the ball beautifully several times and scored the sixth goal.

Jie Hansheng's Final Masterpiece: 194

At this point, although Shanghai tried to get excited, it was impossible to turn the tide. Several attacks failed to break through the solid wall of Tianjin's defense. In the last two minutes, Tianjin's main player, Jie Hansheng, fired a long shot that was unstoppable, entering the net just a few inches below the goalpost, resulting in a final score of 7-1.

Overview of Tianjin and Shanghai's Gains and Losses 195

Although the results were very different, Shanghai's performance was remarkable. Among the forwards, Defei was the most brilliant. Zhou Xianyan's goalkeeping was also highly praised, having saved countless unavoidable dangers. Otherwise, the score would have been even worse. The reason for the defeat was that the strength of the center back and full back lines was insufficient. Tianjin's victory was due to home advantage, familiarity, and even talent. Their excellent teamwork was something that Shanghai could not match. Today, Shanghai will play against the Tianjin Chinese Combined Team.

Jiangda Basketball

Daxia Wins the First Final in the Men's Division Against Jinan 196

Thirty-Four to Twenty-Nine

A Second Final Is Still Needed

The men's basketball championship of Jiangda, Daxia and Jinan, had equal scores, so a final of three games with one win was made. The first final yesterday was held at the China Basketball Stadium, Daxia won Jinan with thirty-four to twenty-five, taking the first step. Due to the panic and tension on both sides, the performance was diminished. The cheering students from both schools in the stadium were very loud. The referees were Li Zuqi and Wu Jiatang.

Both Sides Show Panic 197

Because it was about the championship, both sides showed panic and could not calm down. After the start of the jump ball, people were flustered and confused, unable to grasp or be sure of anything. Even until the end, they could not fully recover their normal state due to the tension of the situation. Jinan's Han Zhenyuan, amidst the chaos, broke through and made a steady throw under the basket, but failed. Three or four minutes later, Daxia's Chen Baoqiu scored two consecutive times, and the record of 4-0 was opened.

Daxia Wavered 198

Jinan found a loophole, retreated to attack, and scored three points. Daxia scored again, Jinan recovered again, making it a 6-6 tie, and then surpassed it with 8-6. At this time, Daxia suddenly showed a wavering state. The full-back general, Guan Dang'an, was penalized out for four fouls. Jinan took this opportunity to jump up, 9-7, 11-8, leading by three or four points for a moment. Fortunately, Daxia fought hard, and the first half ended with an equal score of 19-19.

Jinan Could Not Hold On 199

Starting in the second half, Daxia's momentum improved slightly, but they lost countless certain opportunities. Each scored one goal, making it 21 equal. At this time, Daxia's Ren Jiexing lost a great opportunity for a sneak attack under the basket, and Chen Maiqiu missed consecutive free throws, feeling very frustrated. Jinan, with a throw from Xu Rongshui, turned it into an equal score. Daxia then fully mobilized, their skills gradually became familiar, and Ren Jiexing scored three consecutive goals. Jinan's Wang Nanzhen and Xu Rongshui were successively penalized out, a fatal blow, and they could not hold on. Daxia finally won with thirty-four to twenty-nine, which can be called a hard-fought battle.

Jiangda Volleyball Tournament 200

—A Four-Day Consecutive Tournament Starting on May 7th

—All Venues Are at the China Athletics Field

Rules and Regulations Announced

The Jiangda Volleyball Tournament this year is scheduled to be held for four consecutive days at the China Athletics Field, starting on May 7th. Yesterday, the Jiangda Volleyball Standing Committee announced the schedule and regulations for this year's tournament as follows:

Jiangda Volleyball Championship Regulations 201

(1) A single round-robin system will be used.

(2) The competition dates are set for May 7th, 8th, 9th, and 10th, for four consecutive days. Each team will have two matches each day, the first starting at 10 AM and the second starting at 3 PM (for the women's division, the competition time will be one hour earlier, the first starting at 9 AM and the second starting at 2 PM). The location is the China Athletics Field.

(3) The winning team in each match will receive two points, and the losing team will receive zero points. If the total scores of two teams are equal, a final will be held, with the date to be determined by the committee.

(4) The competition rules will be implemented in accordance with the latest volleyball rules approved by the Chinese National Sports Federation.

(5) Referees will be appointed by the committee, and the competition balls will be purchased by the committee.

(6) If a team does not appear within fifteen minutes of the scheduled competition time, it will be considered a forfeit. However, if the delay is due to unforeseen circumstances en route, it will not be counted.

(7) The competition schedule cannot be changed. However, if the venue is unusable due to rain and postponement is necessary, the committee will make a temporary decision and set a makeup date.

(8) The list of players (limited to fifteen) must be sent to the Chairman of the Volleyball Committee before April 30th, who will forward it to the Review Committee for review.

Anhui Zonal Games 203

—Divide the Province into Six Zones—

The Meeting Period is Set for April 30th or May 7th

The Anhui Education Department yesterday drafted a plan for zonal games and issued an order to its subordinates. The plan is as follows: All public and private secondary schools of the same gender above the provincial and county level in this province are designated as sports zones, with exceptions approved by the department in special circumstances. Counties near each other with one or two schools may contact the host organizations of nearby sports zones to participate, with travel and accommodation expenses borne by themselves. The host organization for each zone will be designated by the department and hosted by the provincial social education organizations or schools, and the host will also convene schools in the area to form a committee. The expenses should not exceed 200 yuan. Each participating school should pay 10 yuan, and members of the public should pay a registration fee. If there are insufficient funds, they should be raised by local organizations. The expenses should only be used for lime, books, stationery, hired labor, and tea, etc. All other sports equipment should be borrowed from the schools. If there is no suitable venue, the police training ground should be borrowed. The meeting period is April 30th or May 7th. Outstanding athletes will be specially trained to participate in the autumn provincial games. The sports events are divided into men's and women's groups. There are fifteen kinds of events for men and ten kinds for women. The prizes are divided into individual and team awards. The province is divided into six zones: 1. Huaining, 2. Wuhu, 3. Fengyang, 4. Hefei, 5. Fuyang, 6) Xiuning. The host organizations for zones 1, 2, and 3 are the sports field and social education organizations run by the province. The host for zone 4 is the Sixth Middle School, the host for zone 5 is the Second Middle School, and the host for zone 6 is the Second Middle School.

The Second Issue of the Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Public Sports Field Quarterly is Published 208

Rich Material ▲ Low Price

The "Sports Research and Communication" quarterly, edited by the Jiangsu Provincial Public Sports Field in Zhenjiang, was well-received nationwide after the publication of the first issue. The second issue has now been published, and the content is even more exciting than before. A closer look at the publication reveals that it focuses on practice and does not advocate empty talk. For example, Ms. Chen Yunlan's Practical Women's Medical Exercises and Pei Xiyuan's Group Skills and Games are all materials that the sports community urgently needs. Wu Bangwei's Sports Refereeing Method and Yuan Zongze's Brief History of the Jiangsu Games are all valuable works. Dong Chengkang's Key Points for Track and Field Competitions and Wu Bangwei's Summary of Recent Sports Rules are essential references for athletes. In addition, various rule questions in the communication column and the general situation of county sports field undertakings are all witty and interesting works. The entire book is over 200 pages long and contains over 150,000 words. It is worthy of being a top sports publication. The retail price is only 30 cents per issue, and the annual subscription for four issues is only one yuan. In order to promote national sports, the field has set a low price to achieve popularization. The Shanghai distributors are the Qinfen Bookstore on Fourth Road or Father Lao Road.

Spring and Autumn

Children Save the Nation 210

— Zhan Lu

Three elementary school students, only fourteen or fifteen years old, from the Guangzhou Municipal Fifty-Fourth Elementary School, determined to join the army and kill the enemy because the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol had fallen one after another. Beforehand, they only told their parents that the school's scout camp required three days of overnight stay. After several days, the school and the parents of each student received letters from the children, stating that they had joined the Nineteenth Route Army to prepare to go north and kill the enemy! Who are the children? Luo Weiquan, Huang Yanxing, and Dong Yuekang, all sons of wealthy merchants from Guangdong and Hong Kong. The letters received by the school have been disclosed in various newspapers in Guangdong and Hong Kong:

Dear Sir, the three provinces have fallen, and Jehol has been lost. All enthusiastic men should save the nation. But, Xue Liang and others abandoned the land and fled. We, students, seeing this, should do our part. So, we joined the army to kill the enemy. We separate from now on, and we will meet again in the next life. With grief and indignation, we cannot say everything! Students Luo Weiquan, Huang Yanxing, and Dong Yuekang together.

Some people, after seeing this letter, appreciated their clear and smooth writing, indeed promising talents. Since they are sons of wealthy merchants, they could work hard in science, study aviation, and when there is a chance in the future, engage in saving the country and killing the enemy, which would certainly be a considerable achievement. Wouldn't that be much better than being underage soldiers now? I say: This is true, but the high-spirited children, when they say save the country, they save the country, with a feeling of "If this is the case, why wait for next year?" One must not use the cautious thinking of adults to criticize the average national salvation children. I am sorry that they are too young for their national salvation determination, but they do what they say, and they do it before they say it, not saying it without doing it. This is the prototype of Wang Yangming's unity of knowledge and action. Compared to the recent speculative soldiers' telegrams of killing the enemy, flying like snowflakes, but in the end, they just run away, alas! Reading the children's letters, how can one not be ashamed to die?

After Children's Day, with these three children who abandoned their pens and joined the army, the value of Children's Day has been greatly enhanced.

Temptation 211

— Held by Buddha

Whenever we pass the entrance of a venereal disease doctor, we often see a shocking advertisement: a beautiful woman's head, whose lower body suddenly transforms into a terrifying poisonous snake, entwined around a young man's body, clinging to him like glue, refusing to let go. If we were to cover the lower half of that beauty's snake body, we would surely say she is an angel from heaven, a rare beauty in the world; if we didn't uncover it and take a look, and saw it was the snake-bodied, human-faced monster mentioned in the Classic of Mountains and Seas, then such an intimate, lingering scene would probably make even Liu Xiahui's heart waver, and cause Lu the Manly Man to experience a "sexual impulse."

On the streets, we often see this phenomenon: when friends are fighting on the road, they are sure to have their factions; during the fight, they might pretend to be "peacemakers," acting with zealous enthusiasm and high righteousness, appointing themselves as Lu Zhonglian. However, when the opportunity arises, they learn the methods of boxing instructors, only saying in their mouths, "We are all family, let's talk it over, why resort to violence?" Little do you know, they'll be impolite and deliver a few cold punches, only they secretly understand which side they are biased towards. Most hilariously, after punching someone a few times, they press their own arm, groaning in pain, claiming to have been injured by the other person. This is a common occurrence in society, nothing too comical.

Aren't the Japanese's specialties and ghostly tricks very similar to the above two scenarios? They clearly understand the weaknesses of us Chinese people, | which are also our bad habits | After plundering the three northeastern provinces and Rehe, they released a lot of hot air to confuse people's minds: what direct negotiations, what military agreements. They even advocated Sino-Japanese cooperation, maintaining peace in East Asia; Sino-Japanese relations returning to their old friendship, avoiding a second world war; isn't this like punching someone a few times and saying, "No fight, no acquaintance?" Isn't this like a female con artist using seductive means to carry out her extortionist tricks? We must not listen to the Japanese's sweet talk, and beware that although they have human faces, they have snake bodies underneath!

The Japanese government's diplomacy completely adopts the "seduction policy" of prostitutes, just like the "smokescreen" used in wartime. This "seduction policy" has anesthetized us forgetful Chinese people, and it is indeed even more dangerous and frightening than a smokescreen! I advise my compatriots who are content with temporary peace, and who are lazy and forgetful, never to fall for the Japanese! I say this because we Chinese people are unusually enthusiastic and energetic about the occurrence of a certain event. For example, newspapers that bear the responsibility of guiding the people, are initially very energetic, using special headline fonts; later, they gradually fade away, using first-class fonts; after a long time, they fade away as if forgotten, and you can't find a single word about it in the entire newspaper! Alas! Is this the phenomenon we are seeing now? I dare not say!

Antiques and Secondhand Goods 212

— Rong Yu

Old copper and rotten iron, moth-eaten books and worm-eaten paintings. Once they enter an antique shop, their value increases tenfold; once they arrive at a secondhand stall, they are worthless. In reality, to speak plainly, they are all old things; they are all shelved goods. Called an antique, it's worth a fortune; changed into secondhand goods, it's not worth a cent. What is the difference there? It's really inexplicable!

The patrons of antique shops are: blue-eyed, blonde foreigners; pot-bellied, wealthy merchants; politicians and military men who have retired from office; hermits who consider themselves loyal. They take a fancy to an item, pay thousands or tens of thousands for it, take it back to appreciate and cherish it, and this old thing is in luck.

The old customers of secondhand stalls are: disheveled and dirty coolies; old soldiers with hunched shoulders; peddlers and laborers in tattered clothes: the deals they make are mostly a few copper coins, and if they spend a few dimes, it's a really big deal. If he has money, he will throw it in the trash can; he won't cherish it or collect it!

Alas! Outdated goods, in luck, become antiques, out of luck, become secondhand goods. Things are like this, let alone people. Look at those with brilliant achievements, leaving their names in history, these are the antiques among people; those who are unappreciated and die old under the window, they are the secondhand goods among people. Success makes a king, failure makes a bandit. The difference between antiques and secondhand goods must be in this.

Even we writers can't escape this example. Some publications become popular as soon as they are published, and the paper is expensive in Luoyang; some are scribbled and smeared, and ultimately belong to the word box. What about racking your brains, what about deliberation, as long as you ask yourself whether you are an antique or secondhand goods? If you are an antique, someone will beg you. If it's secondhand goods, then crying in front of the Emperor Wenchang and the Most Holy Teacher and the old man Cangjie will have no effect.

Alas! Antiques and secondhand goods really cause all kinds of doubts; and add a lot of misery!

The Mystery of the Leather Bag 213

— Zhou Xichang

The leather bag is not the large suitcase you take when traveling to Europe and America, nor is it the wooden box at home for storing clothes, it is a fourteen-inch-long leather satchel used by students as a book bag. When you walk through Ximen, the center where students gather and disperse, you can see many people carrying leather bags, especially in the morning when going to school, or on Zhonghua Road after 4 PM when school is dismissed, in groups of three or five, men in gowns and Western trousers, women in shorts and long cheongsams, except for a triangular or rectangular colored school badge pinned on the front placket, the one they hold in their hands is the leather bag I am talking about.

Some villagers who have just arrived in Shanghai, when they saw it, they said to their companions: "How come there are so many young foreign doctors?"

On the cover of the leather bag, a few fancy English letters are written in lacquer, which turns out to be the full name of the owner of the leather bag, so this can save the trouble of male and female students communicating their names in social interactions, and the busy work of several young masters and young ladies seeking love and secretly checking their names.

Even more so, a group of female students who are slightly lower in grade, the books they read are all thin paper books in Chinese, Party Principles, history, geography, etc., without the embellishment of gold-lettered leather-covered foreign-bound thick books, for the sake of being fashionable, they have to patronize the leather bag that costs three silver dollars a piece.

Therefore, before and after the start of each semester, the bosses of those leather suitcase stores rush to produce them day and night, and it is not enough to meet the market demand.

As for the other mysteries of the leather bag, I will have to ask those who have leather bags to tell you themselves.

Long Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 214

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: Love Resumes in the Teahouse, Difficult New Year at the Pawnshop

Gui Zhi said: But we still owe him money from last year, maybe he deducted it. We don't have any children at home, do we need this honey offering? It's not a big deal. Jiang Shi said: Even though you say that, offering to Heaven and Earth and our ancestors is a once-a-year thing, and if we can't even do it, people will laugh at us, saying we're really not like a proper family. Gui Zhi said: Let's calculate how much money people outside owe us, we should go collect it. Today is the twenty-sixth, and this month is a short one, meaning it's almost New Year's Eve. Gui Zhi said: I calculated it a long time ago, it's only two or three dollars. It's useless to ask for it. We should wait for old Li from the village to send money. Jiang Shi said: This old Li is also taking advantage of us orphans and widows. The money that should have been given in the ninth and tenth months isn't even enough now. If he doesn't send it today, I'll have to get up early tomorrow and go find him. Gui Zhi said: You should have gone a long time ago. The New Year is coming soon, and there's no money for anything, what are you going to do on New Year's Eve? Jiang Shi was already full of worries. After her daughter said this, she became even more anxious. She waited until late that day, but didn't see old Li send any money. Jiang Shi didn't sleep well all night. The next day, she got up early and hired a donkey to go to the village. At three or four o'clock in the afternoon, Jiang Shi returned home with a dusty face, clear snot frozen and streaming down her face, looking dejected. Gui Zhi rushed to ask: How's the money? Jiang Shi sat on the bed, and after a long while, she said: Let me catch my breath before I tell you. Seeing this, Gui Zhi guessed that she probably didn't get the money, and didn't dare to say much, fearing it would make her mother even angrier. After a while, Jiang Shi poured a cup of hot water from the stove and drank it, then wiped her face, and then went outside to brush off the dirt from her body before walking back into the inner room and saying: Look, isn't this killing us? Old Li went to Baoding a month ago and hasn't returned to this day. I couldn't stand it anymore, so I said, in that case, don't even think about celebrating the New Year, I'm going to take my child and stay at his house for a few days. His daughter-in-law got anxious, and only then did she take out five dollars to teach me to take back and use first. She also asked many people to come out and speak for me. (43)

Children's Paradise

Several Toys 215

— Zhu Lu

Prelude

I dare not say that our country's family education is so bad; but because the family pays too little attention to the children's toys, the children's knowledge, such as the skills of playing mahjong, which is all about winning, are more sophisticated and popular than any other knowledge! Mahjong can practice mental arithmetic, which is not a bad toy, but the people who play mahjong use it as a tool for gambling money, and some people stay up all night, indulging in it. This bad influence, instilled into the pure minds of children, is more harmful than beneficial. Therefore, children's toys must be found outside of mahjong. The following types, although common toys, can exercise the body, increase intelligence, and are cheap and easy to make. Children in any family can enjoy them. Now I specially write them out to offer to my dear children.

Jianzi and Diabolo

In these years, we must prepare for how to deal with the "arrival of the worst environment" and exercise our physique, which is the most needed course. Therefore, the kind of "ping pong" and "tennis" that can exercise the physique are all beneficial games for children. But the simplest toy in the family that is good for the body is the jianzi and the diabolo. The method of making jianzi is very simple: use a large steel coin, sew it with cloth, and sew a chicken feather tube on it; after sewing, insert three or four rooster tail feathers into the tube, and the jianzi is made. (Some use paper to make it, the method is also very simple). The way to play jianzi is mostly by kicking it with the foot. In addition to the most common right foot kick, there are also various styles such as combined plate (kicking with both feet), turning, leaping, and jumping. The lively jumping can not only practice leg strength, but also activate all parts of the body. There are single-headed and double-headed diabolos, which are sold in the market and are very cheap. Playing the diabolo can not only exercise the muscles and bones of the whole body, but also emit a pleasant ringing sound; after playing it skillfully, you can also throw it up and down to create new tricks.

Tangram and Puzzle

In addition to building blocks and chess pieces, the tangram and puzzle are indeed also gifts from children that can increase intelligence. The structure of the tangram: there are two large triangles, two small triangles, one medium triangle, and two oblique acute angles and squares; large and small, a total of seven pieces, so it is called "tangram" (Tangram and books about it are sold in the Commercial Press. The tangram is also easy to make by yourself, take a square mahogany, or glass, hard cardboard is also acceptable, a flat hard object, draw diagonally, add a little procedure, 丨 see the picture 丨 is complete.) can be assembled into various utensils and figure forms. The structure of the puzzle is more complicated, with a total of fifteen pieces (see Figure 2) of different sizes of sharp oblique squares and circles, so it feels exquisite and lifelike to assemble it into utensils and figures. Now I have drawn some things about the puzzle on the top. Children, you may also imitate to create a few styles, and you will definitely feel endless interest!

Free Talk

Thoughts on the "Sexual Desire Problem of Prisoners" 216

— Zhu Xiuxia

Ever since Dr. Zhang advocated sexology, the world has been in turmoil. Now this old man has returned from "sex" to "farming," as if the sex craze has subsided, and not many people are advocating the "sex" problem anymore. But in the past few days, a certain legislative member has brought up the issue of prisoners' sex on the news. After all, elegant music has a lingering quality, which makes me solemnly admire him!

The member doesn't think much about the group in hell, but focuses on sexual desire, which is called seeing the hidden and benefiting the subordinates. As usual, it also belongs to the emperor's vast grace.

However, I don't understand other things very well, but I have had a glimpse into prisons. As far as I know: the criminals in prison do not feel any sexual distress. On the contrary, the oppression of hunger and cold, and the suffocation of death, are what they endure. Because all prisons, even those that claim to be "model" prisons, the prisoners only eat twenty-four ounces of grains, mixed with chaff, sand, and stone, and two chopsticks of smelly root vegetables every day. They live in a damp small room (a "cell" of less than seven feet square, where two or three people live). In winter, the bedding that can be issued by chance is an old and broken blanket like a spider web. In summer, in a cell full of sweat and stench, they are like steamed buns in a steamer. People living in this living hell become half-dead in less than a year or two. Because they don't have enough nutrition and lack air and exercise, the sexual desire problem that the adults are concerned about can be said to be simply irrelevant.

However, this is not surprising. The adults go out in cars, eat big meals, and live in Western-style houses. In such a well-fed life, women are naturally considered the only important thing. There was an emperor who asked starving people why they didn't eat meat porridge? It's not unreasonable for the adults to pay attention to the sexual desires of prisoners. Moreover, "according to the law," "imitating the West," speaking with logic, and discussing with evidence, it is indeed feasible. Unfortunately, I don't know if it is because the bodies of Chinese people are worse, or if there are other reasons, but I always feel that this opinion is a bit like joking.

Although it is, "food and sex are human nature," as the sages said, but for those who are not as well-fed as the adults, the problem of sexual desire does not seem necessary. If prisoners were given a chance for temporary freedom, then the "freedom" that criminals and non-criminals would demand is more than just indulging the emperor's grace on women. As for saying "no descendants is the greatest unfilial act," this is not true. China's population is already too large, and the traitors that these traitors raise are probably small traitors. In the future, if the "internal" is not stable, there is no way to resist the "external," and at least they will have to be "suppressed" a few times, which is just asking for trouble.

Therefore, it is better for that member to cancel this opinion. I think the prisoners don't care about such grace at all.

"Bachelor Crying for His Wife" and "Tears on the Barren Mountain" 217

— Dezhong

I remember a small thing, which I heard from other people's mouths, but until yesterday, I couldn't find any proof, so I never told anyone else about it.

That was when the ministers of the Manchu Qing Dynasty met with foreign representatives for the first time. The foreigners all sang their own national anthems with "yi yi wu wu." What did our Manchu Qing ministers sing? Everyone stood up and discussed for a long time, and then sang a short tune, probably called "Bachelor Crying for His Wife"! It was so sad and mournful that the yellow-haired devils were confused!

When I heard this, I thought it was impossible. Even if the Manchu Qing government was corrupt and the officials were confused, it would not be so bad.

Now, our artistic star Cheng Yanqiu, who "self-funded" a trip to France to study art, has returned to China. In his conversation with reporters, he said:

I did not perform dramas in Germany and France. ... Only at the opening of the International New Education Conference in July last year, as usual, each country's national anthem had to be played before the representative's speech. Before the speech of our country's representative, I sang a section of "Tears on the Barren Mountain." There was no erhu, no drum, just a dry song, which was something I had never done in my life.

So I can't help but believe that "Tears on the Barren Mountain" can represent "national anthem," and "Bachelor Crying for His Wife" can certainly represent "national anthem."

But the point to note here is, what is "Tears on the Barren Mountain"? It is an opera based on the "tyrannical government is fiercer than a tiger" in the Tan Gong chapter of the Book of Rites. The father-in-law and husband are all dead, leaving only a small widow, sadly and mournfully "crying." This little widow is Cheng's signature role. Of course, singing such a "signature role" with "no erhu, no drum, just a dry song," how much of a condescension for Cheng's great talent!

Before it was crying for a wife, now it is crying for a husband, which is comparable before and after, but unfortunately the yellow-haired foreign devils are just as confused!

The Death of Bai Yutang 218

— Shiheng

Recently, I read "Three Heroes and Five Gallants" and its sequel, and saw that many Chinese moral values and traditional thoughts are clearly expressed in these books, and undoubtedly these stale moral thoughts have dominated the Chinese readers for hundreds of years. The most obvious example is the death of Bai Yutang.

The thoughts of the authors who wrote books like "Three Heroes and Five Gallants" can be simply explained in a few words. What they unanimously praised was "loyalty, filial piety, integrity, and righteousness," what they hated to the bone was "adultery, theft, and evil," and at the same time what they wanted to express in their stories was "retribution is a cycle, heaven's principles are infallible." And for them, the ultimate retribution for mankind is death, especially "violent death."

Therefore, all chivalrous people ended up being granted official positions, glorifying their families, and they must have very kind descendants. Those evildoers were either arrested and executed, or they must die under random knives. But in the case of Bai Yutang, it is a unique example.

Bai Yutang, nicknamed the Brocade-Coated Rat, is one of the most important characters, one of the five rats, and because of his prominent personality (most of the characters in this type of book have no personality), he is a very lively and lovely character. What is his personality like? According to the author, he is "arrogant and self-willed." This kind of temper is nothing now, but for an author with such traditional thoughts, a person who is not smooth in dealing with the world, who does not give in to others in everything, who does not obey others in everything, this is terrible, he should be given retribution, so Bai Yutang, although he is a righteous man, had to die.

Bai Yutang explored the Chongxiao Tower three times and died under random arrows. His body was "like a hedgehog," which was really unbearable to witness. If this death is explained based on Bai Yutang's character, it may be touching and make readers feel more in line, but the author did not do so. He ultimately had to bring out the great truth of the cycle of retribution, and through the mouth of the deceased's sworn brother Jiang Ping, he said these words:

"Speaking of our fifth brother, he is really pitiful: this is also because of his usual sinister and harsh behavior, so he suffered this tragic death."

In addition to the death of Bai Yutang, there are two or three other deaths of chivalrous heroes, which also convey the same thoughts of these authors. In the seventy-ninth chapter of the fourth volume of "Sequel to Little Five Gallants," two righteous men who had just been granted official positions also suffered violent deaths, one was Han Liang, nicknamed Overcloud Eagle; the other was Xiong Wei, nicknamed Jade-Faced Cat; they were killed for stealing back the lost clothes and crowns for the emperor in the Cangzhen Tower. The reason for their death was also said through the mouths of the characters in the book.

"Grandpa Zhi (that is, the Black-Eared Fox Zhihua) said: "You don't know about that. These two people are being punished."

"Xu Liang asked: "What is being punished?"

"Grandpa Zhi said: "You don't know about that. When the three of them were the village masters on the Jiafeng Mountain, Xiong Wei brought his family to the mountain, and Han Liang thought it was inconvenient for women to go out, so he forcibly had the minions move out the statue of the Jade Emperor in the Jade Emperor Pavilion and throw it into the mountain stream. This Jade Emperor Pavilion was counted as the back stronghold, and the women lived there. Later, when Xiong Wei came back, he should not have followed them; but he didn't want to hurt the feelings of his brothers. Among them, Peng Yu repeatedly told them not to use the Jade Emperor Pavilion as the back stronghold, but these two people would not listen. When the priest Wei Dao came the next day, the Jade Emperor Pavilion had already been changed to the back stronghold; the priest had no choice but to chant Amitabha three times facing the back. Do you think this retribution is real or not? Xiong Wei, Han Liang, and Peng Yu are life-and-death friends, why is it just Xiong Wei and Han Liang, where did Peng Yu go? If he came, he would have died here too. It shows that people must have good hearts, and the gods and Buddhas must be respected."

Bai Yutang's death still has an internal relationship with his character that can be explained, but the deaths of these two people have nothing to do with themselves. In order to convey the idea of respecting gods, the author had to make them suffer tragic deaths. (To be continued)

Juju Ramblings 219

— Zizhan

(19) Dai Dongyuan's Philosophy

Dr. Hu Shi alone respected Dai Zhen among the thinkers of China in the last three hundred years. He wrote a book called "Dai Dongyuan's Philosophy," which was published by the Commercial Press, and also wrote an article called "Several Anti-Neo-Confucian Thinkers," which was included in the third collection of Hu Shi's essays. The article states that Dai was a scientist, good at mathematics, and proficient in textual research, so his research methods were the most precise, and his philosophy was a philosophy with a scientific spirit. As for why Dai had this thought? Why did he have this philosophy? Dr. Hu has yet to explain. Dr. Hu wrote an article on the New Life, teaching people to always ask "why" in everything, and said that "the difference between humans and animals lies in this 'why'." I wonder why Dr. Hu forgot his "why" teachings when talking about Dai Dongyuan's philosophy. "Taiyan's Speech Records" has a lot of explanations as to why Dai Dongyuan opposed Neo-Confucianism, and it is a pleasure to read. It is recorded here:

Although Mr. Dongyuan specialized in Confucianism, he did not agree with the Song Confucians, and often said, "The law kills people, but it can still be saved; Neo-Confucianism kills people, and there is no way to save it." Because at the end of the Manchu Yongzheng period, the Manchu Yongzheng's red-approved edicts, when blaming his subordinates, did not use the words of the law, but always said, "Where is your conscience? Can you ask yourself without shame?" With just these few words of Song Confucian Neo-Confucianism, he could kill people arbitrarily. People always say that Yongzheng treated people the most cruelly, but they don't know that it was Neo-Confucianism that helped him. Therefore, Mr. Dongyuan cried bitterly and made a small booklet (referring to the book "Mencius's Meaning of Words Explained"). His book did not explicitly scold the Manchus, but seeing his book, no one did not deeply hate the Manchus.

I will send this remotely to Dr. Hu, who likes to ask "why," and ask why Mr. Dai Dongyuan wanted to oppose Neo-Confucianism. As for whether Mr. Taiyan's words have any basis, I also hope that someone who has a textual research addiction and a historical addiction like Dr. Hu Shi can tell me.

Long Creative Work

The Crossroads of Era and Love 220

— Zhang Ziping

"Then shall I go call someone to repair it?"

Haiquan eagerly stood up, volunteering.

"Don't go. Someone has been called."

She smiled and reached out to stop him.

"Who called them?"

"Mr. Zhu. He came to see Ah Cao just now. I troubled him to call them."

Haiquan often heard Qiuying mention someone named Zhu, which inevitably aroused his suspicion of them. Therefore, he was silent for a while, just sitting and daydreaming.

"Mr. Lin, what are you thinking about?"

"Nothing."

He immediately felt that she had already guessed his thoughts.

The sky grew darker. He could no longer clearly see the contours of her face. Because of his experience from earlier in the day, he moved closer to her face again, but at the same time, he cursed his own baseness. Qiuying just smiled and gave him a kiss without any resistance. He felt that her movements were not as passionate as they had been earlier, and her spirit seemed very tired. As soon as he left her, he heard footsteps on the stairs outside.

"Is that Uncle Zhu?"

Her clear voice.

"Yes, it is."

A dull voice from outside.

Haiquan saw a young man leading an electrician into the room. But he could not clearly see their faces.

"Mr. Lin, hold this for me..."

Haiquan had just taken the child when he smelled a stench of urine. He saw Qiuying walk up to the man named Zhu, pull his hand, and they went out together. Their attitude further aroused Haiquan's suspicion.

Before long, the electric light was on, and the child in Haiquan's arms began to cry. Qiuying and the young man named Zhu returned to the room together. Haiquan carefully looked at him. He was a little shorter and fatter than Haiquan, and his body seemed sturdier. He had a pale, white face, and at first glance, he did indeed look like a handsome man. But his eyes were small, and on closer inspection, his figure seemed a little bloated, completely like a little white elephant.

Commercial News

Foreign Exchange and Gold Transactions Thin, River Prices Rise 221

Yesterday was the second day of the customs closure. The banks had no transactions of note. The interbank foreign exchange rate in the market remained at two cents in both the morning and afternoon sessions. There were also not many interbank bill transactions, with over 4.5 million in the morning session and over 700,000 in the afternoon session. Transactions in the small general association amounted to over 400,000. The money shops mainly settled public foreign exchange bills, as it was the first day of the fifteenth period, so settlements were slightly more numerous, totaling over 39 million. Remittances from all routes amounted to over 400,000. Talking About New Tea in Late Spring

Wen Tea Merchants Decreasing, Not Increasing 241

In the future, mountain prices may fall, and there may be a turnaround in overseas tea markets, which may become more active. At this time, there is no expansion of new situations.

Huizhou New Tea is Already Green 242

Red and green teas in Qimen, Zhide, Wuyuan, Xiuning, and Shexian in Anhui Province used to sprout mostly before the Qingming Festival due to the warm climate in the past. In recent years, the climate in the producing areas has become colder, and tea buds have developed later than before. Since the end of last month, the weather has been extremely cold, like severe winter. The tea trees have been held back by the cold and cannot sprout in time. However, recently, the weather has suddenly turned warm, and it has been raining for days. The tea trees in the gardens have been nourished by the warmth and moisture, and the branches have revealed green buds. According to agriculturalists, tea trees in barren and old land were severely damaged by the severe cold of last winter. The trees have more dead, yellow, and old leaves on the branches and will not fully develop this year. It is expected that the yield of these damaged tea trees will definitely not be high. If the weather is abnormal in the future and cannot be remedied in order, the harvest will inevitably be affected.

Amateur Musings

Further Discussion on the Root Cause of China's Problems (Part 1) 244

— Pu

The last "Amateur Musings" mentioned that the root cause of China's problems lies in the fact that the vast majority of the country's people do not have enough to eat and are heading towards starvation and national demise. Although not having enough to eat is a common symptom in various large and small powerful countries today (it is said that there are no unemployed people in the Soviet Union, which should be an exception. I dare not flatter the Red allies, but that is the fact), the Northeast and Jehol have been occupied one after another. A powerful neighbor has already entered the house, but a portion of the national populace and the majority of government leaders still complain and blame heaven, and they continue to fight for profit as before, displaying a tendency to not know to rise up and save themselves until death. This kind of strange symptom that completely lacks national consciousness is unique to our China. If the reason for this symptom is not clarified, we will never be able to extricate ourselves from death.

We believe that the formation of this special symptom can be attributed to the following two reasons:

(1) The bankruptcy of various systems that maintain national consciousness;

(2) The culture that maintains national independence is gradually disappearing.

We know that the independence and greatness of a nation depend entirely on the existence of various political, social, or religious systems that maintain the unity of that nation. A certain system, even if it is conservative and does not conform to political or economic trends, as long as it is used properly and can continue to be improved, will not harm the independence and greatness of the nation. For example, the survival of the Jewish people and the struggle of the Indian nation depend entirely on the maintaining power of their religious systems. Although the British political system still has the name of the emperor, it does not harm the development of his democratic spirit. In addition, such as the dictatorship in Italy and the recent political changes in Germany, although many scholars criticize how backward or regressive they are based on democratic or socialist standpoints, they still represent an independent system of national consciousness. If this system is harmful to the development of the nation, a new system will naturally emerge to replace it, without harming the independence and greatness of the nation. What is the current situation in our China? The existing (imitating others') political system has a name but lacks actual spirit. The economic system is subject to the aggression of capitalist imperialism from the outside and the influence of political chaos from the inside. Therefore, the original rural system, handicraft system, and family system that maintained national economy and slightly maintained national consciousness are gradually disappearing and heading towards bankruptcy. In addition, the religious system has no special influence in China, so we feel that the first reason for the special symptoms of China today is the bankruptcy of the system. There is no good system, no system that conforms to the trend, and no bad system, no backward system either. For example, the autocratic regime of the Manchu Qing Dynasty, as a backward system, was destined to be crushed and destroyed by the wheels of the times, which is an iron fact and cannot be denied. However, the autocratic system, even as bad as that of the Manchu Qing, did not completely lose the solemn discipline inherent in the system itself. You see that after the naval commander Ding Ruchang lost the battle of the Sino-Japanese War, he still knew the law of responsibility and could resolutely commit suicide to atone for his country and apologize to the people. In fact, precisely because if he did not commit suicide, he would not be able to avoid death. On this point alone, it can be said that the system itself has not shown complete bankruptcy. But today is different. The responsible parties for the loss of several provinces can still leisurely travel overseas amidst the cheers of important figures. The government has no intention of punishing them, and the public has no power to sanction them. Therefore, the bankruptcy of the entire political and social system can be said to be completely exposed.

We know that the promotion of a national spirit and its ability to strive for survival must all rely on the leadership of a system. Without a system, its operational effectiveness will be lost, and the self-confidence in national struggle will gradually disappear. We feel very painfully that the current situation of the Chinese nation is very close to this trend. Regarding the second reason for the special symptoms of China today, due to space limitations, we will leave it for discussion in the next "Amateur Musings."

Interview Record of Three Prominent Figures in the Business World

How Xi Guansheng Succeeded 245

— Jia Xiang

From the perspective of the modern world, it can be said that Xi Guansheng, who started as an apprentice and achieved his current status, is a success story. Although this success was due to objective circumstances, his own spirit of hard work is worthy of our analysis and study.

He came to Shanghai as an apprentice more than twenty-five years ago, and now he is the owner of Guanshengyuan with a capital of 300,000. To study the reasons for his success, the following points are essential:

First, fighting against failure: In the process of his initial entrepreneurship, there were two failures. The first was in Nanshi, and the second was on Nanjing Road, both food shops closing down. The difficulties and hardships experienced during that time were truly indescribable. However, when he formed the Guanshengyuan Food Company for the third time, although the capital was only a few hundred yuan, he was able to change his previous exaggeration and adopt a down-to-earth approach, starting from small things as his business policy, and finally succeeded. This experience of "starting from small things" can be said to be a lesson learned from two failures.

Second, attending the university of society: Xi Guansheng once said in a speech about his learning spirit that he had also attended a university, but not a national or public one, but the university of society. He had been to Peiping and Nanjing. Every time he went to a place, he would study the local food and analyze the tastes of the local people to produce food that suited their needs. Therefore, Peiping and Nanjing were his universities. From this point of view, on the one hand, it proves his spirit of learning and research, and on the other hand, it also proves that his success is based on social needs.

Third, treating shop assistants equally: This is also very important to Xi Guansheng's success. He treats all the staff in the shop not only kindly but also equally. Not only equally, but also educating the staff. Because of this, the staff of Guanshengyuan were able to help him succeed and promote his success. At the same time, the large amount of profit he earned was not entirely put into his own pocket, but a lot was distributed to the staff.

A person like Xi Guansheng is indeed a good model for apprentices and shop assistants. His diligence, fearlessness of difficulties, and the spirit of sharing food with everyone are indeed something that ordinary people cannot do. At the same time, he is also very simple in his self-sufficiency, wearing old cloth robes, cloth shoes, etc., maintaining the same state as before his success. This is indeed something that ordinary people find difficult to learn and difficult to do!

Public Life

The Women's Movement in Baihu Village 246

— Gu Guiqiu

Female Salt Vendors

Baihu Village is a village with a dozen or so families living in the middle of a valley. People near Baihu Village have a saying: "Small Baihu Village, wives support husbands; wives carry salt to sell, men are playing cards." These words reflect that women are not incapable.

Indeed, the women of Baihu Village are strong and their muscles are firm; they do not walk weaker than men. They, regardless of old or young, can carry a load of fifty or sixty catties of white salt. They have always relied on this salt-selling life.
